<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="preface">PREFACE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preface" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This manual is compiled to provide detailed information on the essential tools and technologies designed to support the miraculous journey of pregnancy and childbirth.</p>
<p>The field of maternal healthcare has seen remarkable advancements over the years, and with these developments come the need for clear guidance on the operation, maintenance, and benefits of the specialized equipment that plays a crucial role in ensuring the safety and comfort of both mother and child.</p>
<p>From ultrasounds that offer us the first glimpse of new life to the sophisticated monitors that track vital signs during labor and delivery, each piece of machinery is a testament to the intersection of human care and technological innovation. This manual aims not only to educate but also to instill confidence in clinical engineering students as they navigate the operation of various maternity equipment and their preventative maintenance.</p>
<p>As you turn these pages, I hope you gain valuable insights into the functionalities that make each machine an integral part of maternity wards worldwide. The information within this manual has been compiled from teaching notes of various clinical engineering lectures from Kenya Medical Training College. Remember that these notes are free copyright notes and any lecturer from Kenya Medical Training College is free to use, and I'd greatly appreciate if somebody was to add more information to this manual for the benefits of the students.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)</p>
<p>COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT 2</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="theory">Theory:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#theory" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Introduction to maternity Equipment; types, functions. Layout of maternity department; explanation of maternity department layout, description of the activities in the maternity layout.</p>
<p>Revision of reproductive system; explanation of anatomy and physiology of the reproductive system, description of the process of childbirth, explanation of the abnormalities in the reproductive system, listing of the various equipment in maternities, statement of the hygiene requirement in maternity. Weighing scales; explanation of the principles of operation of different types of baby weighing scales, explanation of the function of main parts of weighing scales, description of the appropriate care and maintenance on weighing scales, listing typical faults in weighing scales, explanation of the appropriate repair techniques of typical faults, description of the calibration procedures on baby weighing scales. Vacuum pumps; description of the function and operation of different suction pumps and their respective parts, explanation of the inspection procedures, explanation of the typical faults, explanation of the repair techniques.</p>
<p>Vacuum extractor; explanation of the principles of operation of vacuum extractors, explanation of the function of main parts of vacuum extractors, description of the appropriate care and maintenance, listing typical faults, explanation of the appropriate repair techniques of typical faults, description of the calibration and safety test on vacuum extractors. Infant incubators; explanation of the medical need of infant incubators, explanation of the principle of operation of different types of infant incubators, explanation of the function of main parts, description of the appropriate care and maintenance, listing typical faults, explanation of the appropriate repair techniques of typical faults, description of the calibration and safety tests on infant incubators.</p>
<p>Foetal monitor; parts, use, operation and maintenance. Baby warmer; parts, use, operation and maintenance. Nebulizer; parts, use, operation and maintenance. Photo-box; parts, use, operation and maintenance.</p>

<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
6</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="introduction-to-maternity-department">INTRODUCTION TO MATERNITY DEPARTMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction-to-maternity-department" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Maternity is the department that takes care of expectant mothers before and during delivery.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="functions-and-need-for-maternity-department-in-a-hospital-facility">Functions and need for maternity department in a hospital facility<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functions-and-need-for-maternity-department-in-a-hospital-facility" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Admits expectant mothers who are about to deliver</li>
<li>Keeps records showing the number of newborn babies and other necessary records.</li>
<li>Cares for expectant mothers together with monitoring their progress.</li>
<li>Operational services to mothers who develops compliations during child birth.</li>
<li>Has a nursery section where prematurely babies are admitted and taken care of.</li>
<li>A child is able to get a legal birth certificate easily.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="layout-of-maternity-department">Layout of Maternity Department<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#layout-of-maternity-department" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Sections and their functions</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-74a3a1c1.jpeg" alt="img-1.jpeg">
Figure 1: Layout of Maternity Department</p>
<ol>
<li>Reception; Opening files, keeping records, discharge and enquiries.</li>
<li>Examination room; Determination of mother's condition during pregnancy, blood pressure measurements (systolic and diastolic) and any other condition.</li>
<li>Post-natal; where recovery is done to mothers after delivery and their health status monitored. Mothers who have delivered are also advised accordingly.</li>
<li>Labour Room; It is a room where expectant mothers who are almost delivering stay i.e. waiting room.</li>
<li>Wash room; where toilets and bathrooms are located.</li>
<li>Sterilizing room; where equipment are sterilized to avoid infection.</li>
<li>General Store: Storage for cloth and linen</li>
</ol>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES -
VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
7</p>
<ol start="8">
<li>Theatre: Mothers who undergo caesarian or assisted deliveries are operated.</li>
<li>Recovery room: Mothers from theatre stays and medical care taken.</li>
<li>Matron’s office: Place where matron in charge keeps her records.</li>
<li>General Staff office: Resting points for doctors and nurses assigned in the ward.</li>
<li>Acute room: Expectant mothers who undergo caesarian section operation are prepared.</li>
<li>Changing room: Where doctors and nurses change.</li>
<li>Nursery: Where premature born babies are monitored to desirable conditions.</li>
<li>Prenatal/Antenatal room: Expectant mothers come for checkups to find out on their health conditions.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="important-sections-in-maternity-department">Important sections in Maternity Department<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#important-sections-in-maternity-department" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="a-prenatal">a) Prenatal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-prenatal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Mothers’ weights are monitored to establish their feeding habits. Their blood pressure are also monitored with their details written down to assist in delivery.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="b-labour-delivery-room">b) Labour/Delivery room<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-labour-delivery-room" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Vital signs of the mother are monitored. Expectant mothers are prepared for delivery by nurses or midwives. Midwives in the delivery room assists the expectant mothers to deliver and separate them after birth.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="c-examination-room">c) Examination room<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-examination-room" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Confirmation of baby’s right position and monitoring of baby’s vital signs and weight.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="d-nursery">d) Nursery<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#d-nursery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This is where prematurely born babies are taken care of after birth, and monitored at infant incubators.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="e-theatre">e) Theatre<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#e-theatre" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Mothers with complications (Unable to push or complications with the reproductive system or fetal position) are taken and assisted to deliver.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="revision-of-reproductive-system">REVISION OF REPRODUCTIVE SYSTEM;<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#revision-of-reproductive-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Explanation of anatomy and physiology of the reproductive system, description of the process of childbirth, explanation of the abnormalities in the reproductive system</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="male-reproductive-system">Male Reproductive System<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#male-reproductive-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The male reproductive system includes the external genitals (the penis, testes and the scrotum) and internal parts, including the prostate gland, vas deferens and urethra. Your fertility and sexual traits depend on the normal functioning of your reproductive system, as well as hormones released from the brain.</p>
<p>The male reproductive system is important for reproduction. It is made of the following parts:</p>
<ul>
<li>Penis — the organ used for urination and sexual intercourse. It has spongy tissue that can fill with blood to cause an erection. It contains the urethra, which carries both urine and semen.</li>
<li>Scrotum — this is a loose bag of skin that hangs outside the body, behind the penis. It holds the testes in place.</li>
<li>Testes (or testicles) — these are a pair of egg-shaped glands that sit in the scrotum, on the outside of the body. They produce sperm and testosterone, which is the main male sex hormone.</li>
<li>Epididymis — this is a highly coiled tube that lies at the back of the testes. All sperm from the testes must pass through the epididymis, where they mature and start to 'swim'.</li>
<li>Vas deferens — this is a thick-walled tube joined to the epididymis. It carries sperm from the epididymis up to the prostate gland and urethra.</li>
<li>Prostate gland — this is a walnut-sized gland that sits in the middle of the pelvis. The urethra runs through the middle of it. It produces the fluid secretions that support and nourish the sperm.</li>
<li>Urethra — this is a tube that extends from the bladder to the external opening at the end of the penis. The urethra carries both urine and sperm.</li>
<li>Seminal vesicles — these are 2 small glands above the prostate gland that make up much of the fluid in semen.</li>
<li>Brain — the brain also has an important role in reproductive function, as it controls the release of sex hormones, and is involved in arousal.</li>
</ul>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
10</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-02f8547f.jpeg" alt="img-2.jpeg">
Figure 2: Male Reproductive System</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="common-problems-of-the-male-reproductive-system">Common Problems of the Male Reproductive System<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-problems-of-the-male-reproductive-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>As with any other part of the human body, things can sometimes go wrong with the male reproductive system, including:</p>
<ul>
<li>Infertility; not able to impregnate a woman, despite having carefully timed, unprotected sex for one year.</li>
<li>Difficulty urinating;</li>
<li>Prostate disease - The three most common forms of prostate disease are inflammation (prostatitis), non-cancerous enlargement (BPH), and prostate cancer (Read more about it at <a href="https://medlineplus.gov/prostatediseases.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://medlineplus.gov/prostatediseases.html</a>)</li>
<li>impotence or erectile dysfunction (the inability to get a satisfactory erection)</li>
<li>Loss of libido or sex drive</li>
<li>Hormone deficiency</li>
<li>Testicular cancer</li>
</ul>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
11</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="female-reproductive-system">FEMALE REPRODUCTIVE SYSTEM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#female-reproductive-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The female reproductive system is the body parts that help women or females:</p>
<ul>
<li>Have sexual intercourse.</li>
<li>Reproduce.</li>
<li>Menstruate.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-are-the-parts-of-the-female-reproductive-system">What are the parts of the female reproductive system?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-are-the-parts-of-the-female-reproductive-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The female reproductive anatomy includes both external and internal parts.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-57088c36.jpeg" alt="img-3.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-1fdae04a.jpeg" alt="img-4.jpeg">
Figure 3: Female Reproductive System</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="external-parts">External parts<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#external-parts" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The function of your external genitals are to protect the internal parts from infection and allow sperm to enter your vagina.</p>
<p>Your vulva is the collective name for all your external genitals. A lot of people mistakenly use the term "vagina" to describe all female reproductive parts. However, your vagina is its own structure located inside your body.</p>
<p>The main parts of your vulva or external genitals are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Labia majora: Your labia majora ("large lips") enclose and protect the other external reproductive organs. During puberty, hair growth occurs on the skin of the labia majora, which also contain sweat and oil-secreting glands.</li>
</ul>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES –
VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT 12</p>
<ul>
<li>Labia minora: Your labia minora (“small lips”) can have a variety of sizes and shapes. They lie just inside your labia majora, and surround the opening to your vagina (the canal that joins the lower part of your uterus to the outside of your body) and urethra (the tube that carries pee from your bladder to the outside of your body). This skin is very delicate and can become easily irritated and swollen.</li>
<li>Clitoris: Your two labia minora meet at your clitoris, a small, sensitive protrusion that’s comparable to a penis in men. Your clitoris is covered by a fold of skin called the prepuce and is very sensitive to stimulation.</li>
<li>Vaginal opening: Your vaginal opening allows menstrual blood and babies to exit your body.</li>
<li>Hymen: Your hymen is a piece of tissue covering or surrounding part of your vaginal opening. It’s formed during development and present during birth.</li>
<li>Opening to your urethra: The opening to your urethra is the hole you pee from.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="internal-parts">Internal parts<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#internal-parts" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Vagina: Your vagina is a muscular canal that joins the cervix (the lower part of uterus) to the outside of the body. It can widen to accommodate a baby during delivery and then shrink back to hold something narrow like a tampon. It’s lined with mucous membranes that help keep it moist.</li>
<li>Cervix: Your cervix is the lowest part of your uterus. A hole in the middle allows sperm to enter and menstrual blood to exit. Your cervix opens (dilates) to allow a baby to come out during a vaginal childbirth. Your cervix is what prevents things like tampons from getting lost inside your body.</li>
<li>Uterus: Your uterus is a hollow, pear-shaped organ that holds a fetus during pregnancy. Your uterus is divided into two parts: the cervix and the corpus. Your corpus is the larger part of your uterus that expands during pregnancy.</li>
<li>Ovaries: Ovaries are small, oval-shaped glands that are located on either side of your uterus. Your ovaries produce eggs and hormones.</li>
<li>Fallopian tubes: These are narrow tubes that are attached to the upper part of your uterus and serve as pathways for your egg (ovum) to travel from your ovaries to your uterus. Fertilization of an egg by sperm normally occurs in the fallopian tubes. The fertilized egg then moves to the uterus, where it implants into your uterine lining.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-are-the-functions-of-the-female-reproductive-system">What are the functions of the female reproductive system?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-are-the-functions-of-the-female-reproductive-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The female reproductive system provides several functions. In addition to allowing a person to have sexual intercourse, it also helps a person reproduce.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)</p>
<p>COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
13</p>
<p>Your ovaries produce eggs. These eggs are then transported to your fallopian tube during ovulation where fertilization by a sperm may occur. The fertilized egg then moves to your uterus, where the uterine lining has thickened in response to the normal hormones of your menstrual cycle (also called your reproductive cycle). Once in your uterus, the fertilized egg can implant into the thickened uterine lining and continue to develop. If implantation doesn't take place, the uterine lining is shed as your menstrual period. In addition, the female reproductive system produces sex hormones that maintain your menstrual cycle.</p>
<p>During menopause, the female reproductive system gradually stops making the female hormones necessary for the menstrual cycle to work. At this point, menstrual cycles can become irregular and eventually stop. You're considered to be menopausal when you've gone an entire year without a menstrual period.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-happens-during-the-menstrual-cycle">What happens during the menstrual cycle?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-happens-during-the-menstrual-cycle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Women of reproductive age (beginning anywhere from 11 to 16 years of age) experience cycles of hormonal activity that repeat at about one-month intervals. With every cycle, your body prepares for a potential pregnancy, whether or not that's your intention. The term menstruation refers to the periodic shedding of your uterine lining when pregnancy doesn't occur that cycle. Many people call the days that they notice vaginal bleeding their "period."</p>
<p>The average menstrual cycle takes about 28 days and occurs in phases. These phases include:</p>
<ul>
<li>The follicular phase (the egg develops).</li>
<li>The ovulatory phase (release of the egg).</li>
<li>The luteal phase (hormone levels decrease if the egg doesn't implant).</li>
</ul>
<p>There are four major hormones (chemicals that stimulate or regulate the activity of cells or organs) involved in the menstrual cycle. These hormones include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Follicle-stimulating hormone.</li>
<li>Luteinizing hormone.</li>
<li>Estrogen.</li>
<li>Progesterone.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="follicular-phase">Follicular phase<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#follicular-phase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This phase starts on the first day of your period. During the follicular phase of the menstrual cycle, the following events occur:</p>
<ul>
<li>Two hormones, follicle stimulating hormone (FSH) and luteinizing hormone (LH) are released from your brain and travel in your blood to your ovaries.</li>
</ul>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
14</p>
<ul>
<li>The hormones stimulate the growth of about 15 to 20 eggs in your ovaries, each in its own “shell,” called a follicle.</li>
<li>These hormones (FSH and LH) also trigger an increase in the production of the hormone estrogen.</li>
<li>As estrogen levels rise, like a switch, it turns off the production of follicle-stimulating hormone. This careful balance of hormones allows the body to limit the number of follicles that will prepare eggs to be released.</li>
<li>As the follicular phase progresses, one follicle in one ovary becomes dominant and continues to mature. This dominant follicle suppresses all of the other follicles in the group. As a result, they stop growing and die. The dominant follicle continues to produce estrogen.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ovulatory-phase">Ovulatory phase<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ovulatory-phase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The ovulatory phase (ovulation) usually starts about 14 days after the follicular phase started (the exact timing varies). The ovulatory phase is the second phase of your menstrual cycle. Most people will have a menstrual period 10 to 16 days after ovulation. During this phase, the following events occur:</p>
<ul>
<li>The rise in estrogen from the dominant follicle triggers a surge in the amount of luteinizing hormone (LH) that your brain produces.</li>
<li>This causes the dominant follicle to release its egg from the ovary.</li>
<li>As the egg is released (a process called ovulation) it’s captured by finger-like projections on the end of the fallopian tubes (fimbriae). The fimbriae sweep the egg into the fallopian tube.</li>
<li>For one to five days prior to ovulation, many women will notice an increase in egg white cervical mucus. This mucus is the vaginal discharge that helps to capture and nourish a sperm on its way to meet the egg for fertilization.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="luteal-phase">Luteal phase<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#luteal-phase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The luteal phase begins right after ovulation and involves the following processes:</p>
<ul>
<li>Once it releases its egg, the empty ovarian follicle develops into a new structure called the corpus luteum.</li>
<li>The corpus luteum secretes the hormones estrogen and progesterone. Progesterone prepares your uterus for a fertilized egg to implant.</li>
</ul>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
15</p>
<ul>
<li>If intercourse has taken place and sperm has fertilized the egg (conception), the fertilized egg (embryo) will travel through your fallopian tube to implant in your uterus. This is how pregnancy begins.</li>
<li>If the egg isn't fertilized, it dissolves in your uterus. Not needed to support a pregnancy, the lining of your uterus breaks down and sheds. This is when your period begins.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-many-eggs-does-a-woman-have">How many eggs does a woman have?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-many-eggs-does-a-woman-have" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You're born with all the eggs you'll ever produce. During fetal development, you have about 6 million eggs. At birth, there are approximately 1 million eggs left. By the time you reach puberty, only about 300,000 remain. The number of eggs you have continues to decline as you age and menstruate each cycle. Fertility also declines with age due to the decreasing number and quality of your remaining eggs.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-does-reproduction-work">How does reproduction work?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-does-reproduction-work" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In humans, female and male reproductive systems work together to reproduce. There are two kinds of sex cells — sperm and eggs. When a sperm meets an egg, it can fertilize it and create a zygote. This zygote eventually becomes a fetus. Both a sperm and an egg are needed for human reproduction.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
16</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="child-birth">Child Birth<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#child-birth" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Childbirth, also known as labour, parturition and delivery, is the completion of pregnancy where one or more babies exits the internal environment of the mother via vaginal delivery or caesarean section.</p>
<p>The most common childbirth method worldwide is vaginal delivery. It involves four stages of labour: the shortening and opening of the cervix during the first stage, descent and birth of the baby during the second, the delivery of the placenta during the third, and the recovery of the mother and infant during the fourth stage, which is referred to as the postpartum.</p>
<p>The first stage is characterized by abdominal cramping or also back pain in the case of back labour that typically lasts half a minute and occurs every 10 to 30 minutes. Contractions gradually become stronger and closer together. Since the pain of childbirth correlates with contractions, the pain becomes more frequent and strong as the labour progresses.</p>
<p>The second stage ends when the infant is fully expelled. The third stage is the delivery of the placenta. The fourth stage of labour involves the recovery of the mother, delayed clamping of the umbilical cord, and monitoring of the neonate. As of 2014, all major health organizations advise that immediately following a live birth, regardless of the delivery method, that the infant be placed on the mother's chest (termed skin-to-skin contact), and to delay neonate procedures for at least one to two hours or until the baby has had its first breastfeeding.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="stages-of-labour">Stages of Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stages-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Labour is divided into four stages – the dilation of the cervix, the birth of the baby, the birth of the placenta and the recovery of the mother and infant.</p>
<p>Some of the signs and symptoms of going into labour may include period-like cramps, backache, diarrhoea and contractions. Braxton-Hicks contractions are sometimes mistaken for labour.</p>
<p>These 'false' contractions usually start halfway through the pregnancy and continue all the way through. You may find these contractions visibly harden and lift your pregnant belly.</p>
<p>It is not known what triggers the onset of labour, but it is thought to be influenced by the hormone oxytocin, which is responsible for causing uterine contractions</p>
<p>For first-time mothers, labour takes around 12 to 14 hours. Women who have undergone childbirth before can expect about 7 hours of labour.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="first-stage-of-labour-dilation">First Stage of Labour (Dilation)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#first-stage-of-labour-dilation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The first stage of labour involves the thinning of the cervix and its dilation to around 10 cm.</p>
<p>The first stage is made up of three different phases:</p>
<p>a) The latent phase – Generally, this stage is the longest and the least painful part of labour.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES -
VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
17</p>
<p>The cervix thins out and dilates zero to three centimeters. This may occur over weeks, days or hours and be accompanied by mild contractions. The contractions may be regularly or irregularly spaced, or you might not notice them at all.</p>
<p>b) The active phase – The next phase is marked by strong, painful contractions that tend to occur three or four minutes apart, and last from 30 to 60 seconds. The cervix dilates from 3 to 7–8 centimeters.</p>
<p>c) The transition phase – During transition, the cervix dilates from 8 to 10 centimetres (that is, fully dilated). These contractions can become more intense, painful and frequent. It may feel as though the contractions are no longer separate, but running into each other. It is not unusual to feel out of control and even a strong urge to go to the toilet as the baby’s head moves down the birth canal and pushes against the rectum.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="second-stage-of-labour-expulsion">Second stage of Labour (Expulsion)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#second-stage-of-labour-expulsion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The second stage of labour is from when your cervix is fully dilated to the time your baby is born. The contractions during this time are regular and spaced apart. As each contraction builds to a peak, the mother feel the urge to bear down and push. The sensation of the baby moving through the vagina is described as a stretching or burning, particularly as the baby’s head crowns (appears at the vaginal entrance)</p>
<p>At the time of birth, a doctor or midwife may guide pushing to enable a gentle, unhurried birth of your baby's head. Sometimes the umbilical cord is wound around the baby's neck. If possible, the doctor or midwife will loosen it, loop it over baby's head, or clamp and cut it to allow the baby to be born safely.</p>
<p>Once the head has emerged, midwife or doctor will guide baby’s body so the shoulders come out. The rest of the baby will then follow.</p>
<p>If this is your first baby, the second stage of labour can last up to 1 to 2 hours, particularly if you have had an epidural. If you have had a baby before, this stage is often much quicker.</p>
<p>Monitoring of mother’s condition and that of your baby is increased during the second stage of labour. A long second stage of labour can result in risks for you and your baby. If your labour is not progressing, it is important that the reason is worked out and steps are taken to help the mother.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="third-stage-of-labor">Third Stage of Labor<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#third-stage-of-labor" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)</p>
<p>COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
18</p>
<p>After the birth of the baby, the uterus gently contracts to loosen and push out the placenta, although you may not be able to feel these contractions. This may occur 5 to 30 minutes after the birth of the baby.</p>
<p>The muscles of the uterus continue to contract to stop the bleeding. This process is always associated with a moderate blood loss – up to 500 ml.</p>
<p>In this stage of labour, one of the potential problems is excessive bleeding (postpartum haemorrhage), which can result in anaemia and fatigue. This is why the third stage is carefully supervised.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="fourth-stage-postpartum">Fourth stage: postpartum<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fourth-stage-postpartum" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The fourth stage of labour is the period beginning immediately after childbirth, and extends for about six weeks. The terms postpartum and postnatal are often used for this period. The woman's body, including hormone levels and uterus size, return to a non-pregnant state and the newborn adjusts to life outside the mother's body.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
19</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="weighing-scales">WEIGHING SCALES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#weighing-scales" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Measuring patient’s weight is an important part of monitoring health as well as calculating drug and radiation doses. It is therefore vital that scales continue to operate accurately.</p>
<p>Weighing scales can be used for all ages of patients and therefore vary in the range of weights that they measure.</p>
<p>These scales can be arranged for patients to stand on, or can be set up for weighing wheelchair bound patients (adults).</p>
<p><strong>For infants</strong>, the patient can be suspended in a sling below the scale (spring type) or placed in a weighing cot on top of the scale (electronic type) during the weight measurement.</p>
<p>Baby weighing scales with mechanical scales have a spring that is deflected by patient’s (baby) weight. The spring pushes a pointer along a display or rotates a disc to indicate weight.</p>
<p><strong>Electronic weighing scales</strong> have a sensor that bends under the patient’s weight and the circuitry converts this to displayed digits.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-mechanical-weighing-scales-work">How Mechanical Weighing Scales Work<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-mechanical-weighing-scales-work" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A hook/ spring or hanging scale operates on a principle based on Hooke's Law. This law states that "the force exerted on a spring is directly proportional to the distance it moves as a result of the force. This is represented in the form of the equation,  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="bold">F</mi><mo>=</mo><mi mathvariant="bold">k</mi><mi mathvariant="bold">X</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathbf{F} = \mathbf{k}\mathbf{X}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6861em;"></span><span class="mord mathbf">F</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6944em;"></span><span class="mord mathbf">kX</span></span></span></span></span> , where  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="bold">F</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathbf{F}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6861em;"></span><span class="mord mathbf">F</span></span></span></span></span>  is the amount of force applied to the spring,  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="bold">X</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathbf{X}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6861em;"></span><span class="mord mathbf">X</span></span></span></span></span>  is the distance traveled, and  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="bold">k</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathbf{k}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6944em;"></span><span class="mord mathbf">k</span></span></span></span></span>  is the constant stiffness of the particular spring."</p>
<p>The spring pushes a pointer along a display or rotates a disc to indicate weight of the patient due to the force/weight exerted by the patient (baby).</p>
<p>Beam balances use an application of the lever principle which states that "the further away the counterweight is from the fulcrum, the more downward force it exerts.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="modern-weighing-scales-electronic">Modern Weighing Scales (Electronic)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#modern-weighing-scales-electronic" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Majority of modern scales work by use of devices known as load cells to measure weights of objects, whether being used in medical, industrial or retail set ups.</p>
<p>A load cell is a force gauge that is made up of a transducer that is used to create an electrical signal whose magnitude is in direct proportion with the force being measured.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES -
VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
21</p>
<p>Essentially, when any weight is placed on the scale, the load cell bends slightly; this causes the electrical signal that runs through the load cell to change. The <strong>signal change</strong> is due to the amount of electrical resistance that the bending causes to the strain gauge inside the load cell.</p>
<p>The signal is then read by an electronic device, often a <strong>digital weight indicator</strong>, and transformed into a digital weight value. The value is then displayed for reading in terms of weight.</p>
<p><strong>NB</strong>: Since a load cell essentially measures mass by converting the deformation caused by the load to an electronic signal, <strong>it is sensitive to accidental deformation</strong>, such as shocks or temperature changes. That's why it's essential to treat weighing instruments with care and to calibrate them frequently.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="baby-weighing-scale">Baby Weighing Scale<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#baby-weighing-scale" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A baby weighing scale is specifically-designed to monitor the progress of a baby’s physical development.</p>
<p>If a baby is born prematurely, it is often important to closely monitor their weight gain with a baby scale, more often than for on-time babies. A major difference with the adult scale is that the baby cannot stand on his/her own, special constructions have been created for this. For children who can stand independently, an adult scale is used.</p>
<p>Because babies have a lower weight and weight is an important indicator of growth (and malnutrition) baby scales must be able to measure more accurately.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="65feba40">Why Baby’s Weight is Measured<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#65feba40" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i) To control feeding of the baby
ii) To control the weight of the baby
iii) To determine growth and development of the baby
iv) To monitor health conditions of the baby</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT 22</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types-of-baby-weighing-scales">Types of Baby Weighing Scales<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-baby-weighing-scales" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>i) Spring Balance
ii) Beam balance
iii) Electronic baby weighing scale</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="requirements-for-baby-weighing-scales">Requirements for Baby Weighing Scales<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#requirements-for-baby-weighing-scales" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>i) Should of table top type
ii) Should be light and portable
iii) Should be easy to clean
iv) Should have zero weight adjustment facility
v) Should be of non-metallic tray
vi) Its measurement of weight should not change with position of the pan</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="main-parts-of-weighing-scale">Main Parts of Weighing Scale<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#main-parts-of-weighing-scale" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="setting-of-baby-weighing-scales">Setting of Baby Weighing Scales<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#setting-of-baby-weighing-scales" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>i) Should be on leveled ground/flat surface
ii) The pointer should be indicating zero before weight measurement. This is achieved by zero setting</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="factors-that-can-cause-errors-in-baby-weighing-scales">Factors that can Cause Errors in Baby Weighing Scales<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-that-can-cause-errors-in-baby-weighing-scales" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="difference-between-a-balance-and-a-weighing-scale">Difference between a Balance and a Weighing scale<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#difference-between-a-balance-and-a-weighing-scale" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In basic terms, balances measure mass while scales measuring the weight.</p>
<p>A balance determines <strong>mass</strong> by balancing an unknown mass against a known mass. In modern weighing instruments, balances use a force restoration mechanism that creates a force to balance that exerted by the unknown mass.</p>
<p>A scale displays weight by measuring a deflection; force needed to deform the springs is measured and converted into weight.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="maintenance-care-of-baby-weighing-scales">Maintenance/Care of Baby Weighing Scales<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maintenance-care-of-baby-weighing-scales" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i) Never apply sudden weight on the scales or sudden off load from scales.
ii) Weight on the scale should not exceed its maximum weight.
iii) Cleaning/removing dirt from the scales.
iv) Avoid unnecessary oiling of moving parts.
v) Check all control knobs and balance positioning.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)</p>
<p>COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT 24</p>
