<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="suction-pump-or-machines-aspirators">SUCTION PUMP OR MACHINES (ASPIRATORS)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#suction-pump-or-machines-aspirators" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Suction machine (also known as aspirator) is a type of medical device that is primarily used for removing obstructions like mucus, saliva, blood, or secretions from a person's airway. When an individual is unable to clear secretions due to a lack of consciousness or an ongoing medical procedure, suction machines help them breathe by maintaining a clear airway.</p>
<p>They are found in operating theatres, delivery suites/rooms in maternity department, ENT and emergency departments. Smaller specialized suctions are used in dental departments.</p>
<p>In practice, care professionals use suction machines as an integral part of a treatment plan when a patient's airway is partially or completely obstructed. Some common uses include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Removing respiratory secretions when the patient is unable to.</li>
<li>Assisting a patient that is vomiting while seizing or unconscious.</li>
<li>Clearing blood from the airway.</li>
<li>Removing a foreign substance from a patient’s windpipe and/or lungs (pulmonary aspiration).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="principles-of-operation-of-a-suction-pump">Principles of Operation of a Suction Pump<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-operation-of-a-suction-pump" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Suction is generated by a pump, which is normally an electrically powered motor, but manually powered versions are also often found. The pump generates a suction that draws air from a bottle. The reduced pressure in this bottle then draws the fluid from the patient via a tube. The fluid remains in the bottle until disposal is possible. A valve prevents fluid from passing into the motor itself.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
27</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-b19761a9.jpeg" alt="img-10.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-medical-suction-units-pumps">Types of medical suction Units/Pumps<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-medical-suction-units-pumps" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The suction pump can be either portable or standard. Usually, the standard medical suction pump is connected to the mains electrical supply for energy. Portable suction pumps may be battery operated or they are manually made to create a negative pressure by hand or feet. In addition, they may also use compressed gas as a source of energy.</p>
<p>The many suction pumps in the medical world are categorized according to their features and their use. However, based on the vacuum principle that they operate on, suction pumps may be divided into 4 categories, which include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Electrically Operated Suction Unit</li>
</ul>
<p>It has an Electric motor pump, which is an electrically powered motor that drives a pump to create the required vacuum.</p>
<ul>
<li>Pneumatically driven Suction Unit</li>
</ul>
<p>The pump primarily works on the Venturi principle. The driving force may be attributed to air, stream or water.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)</p>
<p>COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
28</p>
<ul>
<li>A manually operated Suction Unit</li>
</ul>
<p>It is with bellows and unidirectional valves to create the necessary vacuum effectively.</p>
<ul>
<li>Centrally piped suction system</li>
</ul>
<p>i) Manually operated suction unit</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-b81c8c91.jpeg" alt="img-11.jpeg"></p>
<p>It has a piston pump with valves designed for suction or vacuum creation instead of compression or pressure creation.</p>
<p>A clear glass or Perspex bottle with a rubber-sealed lid is included in the pneumatic circuit to reserve the vacuum created.</p>
<p>A flexible rubber or plastic pipe interacts directly with the liquid to be sucked and terminates in the bottle. Another similar pipe leaves the lid to the pump. With each backward stroke, negative pressure is created in the pneumatic system and if the free pipe is immersed in a fluid (e.g. the placental blood and amniotic fluid), the fluid is sucked into the bottle. The bottle is emptied once full. The pump may be designed to be hand operated or foot operated.</p>
<p>N/B: Manual suction unit has the following key parts</p>
<ul>
<li>Bellows/Foot pedals</li>
</ul>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)</p>
<p>COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
29</p>
<ul>
<li>Collecting bottles</li>
<li>Pressure Gauge</li>
<li>Machine and patient suction tubes</li>
</ul>
<p>ii) Electrically operated suction Pump/ unit</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-b1a2c24b.jpeg" alt="img-12.jpeg">
2.5 Major external components of a suction pump.</p>
<p>The pump is operated electrically through an electric motor. The motors may take various forms depending on individual Engineering design and the anticipated capacity of the pump. Popular pump types used include: Centrifugal, reciprocating (piston) and Diaphragm.</p>
<p>A clear glass or Perspex bottle with a rubber-sealed lid is included in the pneumatic circuit to reserve the vacuum created.</p>
<p>A second bottle may be included to boost the pump's capacity to hold sucked fluid which ensures longer suction before emptying is done.</p>
<p>A flexible rubber or plastic pipe interacts directly with the liquid to be sucked and terminates in the bottle. Another similar pipe leaves the lid to the pump. In the two bottle design, the outlet pipe from one bottle goes into the second bottle as input pipe.</p>
<p>The output of the second bottle then goes to the pump. With each backward stroke in the Reciprocating and diaphragm pumps, negative pressure is created in the pneumatic system. In</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES –
VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
30</p>
<p>the Centrifugal type, vacuum is created on the suction pipe which is part of the pneumatic circuit. In all cases if the free pipe is immersed in a fluid (e.g. the placental blood and amniotic fluid), the fluid is sucked into the bottle and the bottles emptied once full. A special float valve (called anti-overflow device) is included in the bottles in some designs. It interacts with the motor control to stop pumping once a pre-determined liquid level is reached.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-b3667854.jpeg" alt="img-13.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-d3d9a283.jpeg" alt="img-14.jpeg"></p>
<p>Flow diagram of electrically operated suction Pump/ unit</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)</p>
<p>COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
31</p>
<p>iii) Central piped vacuum system</p>
<p>This is piped vacuum from a central source. Two motor operated pumps are interconnected to create vacuum in a reservoir. The pumps are operated by pressure switches which activate the pumps once pressure falls below a pre-determined level in the reservoir.</p>
<p>The pump piping is rigid but is connected to the reservoir via a flexible pipe which absorbs the shock of the pumping system before the reservoir during pumping. Outlets to the patient are connected to a central pipe leading to the reservoir. Each patient outlet is connected to the central pipe via a glass bottle trap (for collecting the liquid during suction) and Bacterial filter (for ensuring that pathogenic agents from the suction site and fluid don't pass on to the atmosphere). The air sucked in the system is released to the atmosphere through the exhaust pipe via silencers (which muffle the noise of the gas as it is released under pressure to the atmosphere). A flexible plastic or rubber pipe is connected to the patient outlet on one end and is immersed in the liquid on the other end. The vacuum in the reservoir effects suction of the liquid.</p>
<p>iv) Pneumatic driven Suction Pumps or Vacuum Ejector</p>
<p>A vacuum ejector or simply ejector is a type of vacuum pump, which produces vacuum by means of the Venturi effect.</p>
<p>In an ejector, a working fluid (liquid or gaseous) flows through a jet nozzle into a tube that first narrows and then expands in cross-sectional area. The fluid leaving the jet is flowing at a high velocity which due to Bernoulli's principle results in it having low pressure, thus generating a vacuum. The outer tube then narrows into a mixing section where the high velocity working fluid mixes with the fluid that is drawn in by the vacuum, imparting enough velocity for it to be ejected, the tube then typically expands in order to decrease the velocity of the ejected stream, allowing the pressure to smoothly increase to the external pressure.</p>
<p>The strength of the vacuum produced depends on the velocity and shape of the fluid jet and the shape of the constriction and mixing sections, but if a liquid is used as the working fluid the strength of the vacuum produced is limited by the vapor pressure of the liquid (for water, <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>3.2</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">k</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">P</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">a</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">3.2\mathrm{kPa}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6944em;"></span><span class="mord">3.2</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">kPa</span></span></span></span></span></span> or 0.46 psi or 32 mbar at <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>25</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">25^{\circ}\mathrm{C}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord">2</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">5</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord mathrm">C</span></span></span></span></span> or <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>77</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup><mi mathvariant="normal">F</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">77^{\circ}\mathrm{F}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord">7</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">7</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord mathrm">F</span></span></span></span></span>).</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
32</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="functions-of-medical-suction-pumps">Functions of medical suction pumps<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functions-of-medical-suction-pumps" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Draining blood from operation sites allows the surgeon better visibility.</li>
<li>To drain pus from an abscess</li>
<li>To irrigate the side for washing and sucking out the excess water.</li>
<li>To clean debris from a wound</li>
<li>To suck out Mucus that may be obstructing the airways or other parts of the body.</li>
<li>In gynecological processes to allow better vision and for draining the excess fluid.</li>
<li>In dentistry to drain the blood and the irrigation fluid.</li>
<li>To remove blood from the cranium after an extradural or intracranial hemorrhage.</li>
<li>To suck out foreign bodies from the nose or ear or from other places.</li>
<li>As constant intubation to provide drainage from a surgical site where pus or fluid may collect.</li>
<li>To drain excessive edematous fluid from the peritoneal cavity in patients with ascites.</li>
<li>To drain fluid from the lungs in patients with kidney disease or other major disorders.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types-of-pumps-used-in-suction-units">Types of Pumps used in Suction Units<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-pumps-used-in-suction-units" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Piston pumps</li>
<li>Diaphragm pumps</li>
<li>Rotary pumps</li>
</ul>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT 33</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types-of-motors-used-in-suction-units">Types of Motors used in Suction Units<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-motors-used-in-suction-units" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Commonly for suction pumps, capacitor run motors are used because centrifugal switches (to switch off starting winding and capacitor) cannot be manufactured—sparkless. In suction pumps for operating theatres, sparkless switches have to be used.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="capacitor-run-motor">CAPACITOR - RUN - MOTOR:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#capacitor-run-motor" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-b76af6a5.jpeg" alt="img-15.jpeg"></p>
<p>To the starting winding in series, a capacitor is connected. This causes a phase displacement in the starting winding and in turn a rotating field which causes the rotor to turn.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="single-phase-split-phase-motor">SINGLE PHASE SPLIT PHASE MOTOR:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#single-phase-split-phase-motor" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The higher resistance of the starting winding causes the phase displacement. The starting winding is switched off by the centrifugal switch when the motor attains about 80% of full speed to keep the power factor as high as possible.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="capacitor-start-motor">CAPACITOR - START - MOTOR:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#capacitor-start-motor" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Additional to the starting winding of the single phase split phase motor a capacitor is connected in series to the starting winding to obtain a greater phase displacement.</p>
<p>The centrifugal switch switches off capacitor and starting winding when a certain speed is reached in order to achieve a high power factor.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="shaded-pole-motor">SHADED POLE MOTOR:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#shaded-pole-motor" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The phase displacement is achieved with a starting winding. The starting winding is just one closed turn of a heavy copper wire embedded in one side of the stator.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES — VOLUME 1)</p>
<p>COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT 34</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="vacuum-extraction-delivery">VACUUM EXTRACTION DELIVERY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vacuum-extraction-delivery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction-to-vacuum-extraction-delivery">Introduction to vacuum extraction delivery<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction-to-vacuum-extraction-delivery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>During the second stage of labor, when you're actively trying to push your baby out, sometimes the process of childbirth seems to stall. You're trying, but the baby isn't coming. This can go on for hours. While you're in labor, your healthcare team will monitor your vital signs and your baby's heart rate to stay alert to any signs of fetal distress. If you or your baby's health is in danger from prolonged labor, and labor isn't progressing, your healthcare team will look for ways to assist you in delivering your baby.</p>
<p>Vacuum extraction is one way they can assist. If certain conditions are met — your baby's head is low enough in the birth canal and they're in an appropriate position — a vacuum extractor may be able to help guide them out. The vacuum extractor consists of a suction cup attached to a mechanical or electric pump. The cup is applied to your baby's head and the pump provides traction to pull while you push. It's not always the solution you need, but sometimes it does the trick.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="why-is-vacuum-extraction-used-during-delivery">Why is vacuum extraction used during delivery?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#why-is-vacuum-extraction-used-during-delivery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Vacuum extraction, or "ventouse," is one method healthcare providers use to help get your baby out when they aren't coming out on their own. There are other methods, including forceps delivery and C-section. Usually, surgery is considered a last resort. Vacuum extraction and forceps delivery offer additional ways for healthcare providers to assist laboring mothers before resorting to C-section delivery.</p>
<p>Vacuum extraction and forceps delivery are similar in their advantages and disadvantages, and often the choice between them comes down to the training and experience of your healthcare provider. Both methods carry some risk, but healthcare providers recommend them when the risks of not helping appear to be greater. This might be because either you or your baby are suffering from prolonged labor.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure-details">Procedure Details<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure-details" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="what-are-the-indications-for-vacuum-extraction-delivery">What are the indications for vacuum extraction delivery?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-are-the-indications-for-vacuum-extraction-delivery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Vacuum extraction might be indicated if:</p>
<ul>
<li>Labor is prolonged or stalled in the second stage, and</li>
<li>The baby's heart rate is considered "non-reassuring" or</li>
<li>The mother can't push anymore, either due to exhaustion or a health condition.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="what-does-a-non-reassuring-fetal-heart-rate-mean">What does a "non-reassuring" fetal heart rate mean?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-does-a-non-reassuring-fetal-heart-rate-mean" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Healthcare providers see an abnormal fetal heart rate as a sign that the baby isn't getting enough oxygen during labor. It's normal for oxygen to be restricted temporarily during labor, but if it goes on for too long, it's dangerous to the health of the baby.</p>
<p>Your baby's heart rate might be considered non-reassuring if:</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES -
VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
37</p>
<ul>
<li>It’s abnormally high.</li>
<li>It’s abnormally low.</li>
<li>It has a pattern of abrupt decreases.</li>
<li>It takes too long to return to the baseline rate after a contraction.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-can-we-try-first-before-vacuum-extraction">What can we try first before vacuum extraction?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-can-we-try-first-before-vacuum-extraction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>If your baby’s heart rate indicates possible distress, your healthcare team might first try to compensate by:</p>
<ul>
<li>Giving you oxygen through a mask.</li>
<li>Giving you fluids through a vein in your arm.</li>
<li>Changing your position to facilitate faster delivery.</li>
</ul>
<p>If these interventions don’t improve your baby’s heart rate or advance labor, your healthcare team may recommend an operational procedure such as vacuum extraction.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-are-the-contraindications-for-vacuum-extraction">What are the contraindications for vacuum extraction?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-are-the-contraindications-for-vacuum-extraction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Sometimes you might need assistance, but vacuum extraction isn’t the right choice. This might be true if your baby:</p>
<ul>
<li>Is premature.</li>
<li>Has not progressed low enough in the birth canal.</li>
<li>Might not fit through the birth canal.</li>
<li>Is not positioned headfirst.</li>
<li>Needs to be rotated.</li>
<li>Has a bleeding disorder.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-happens-during-a-vacuum-extraction-delivery">What happens during a vacuum extraction delivery?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-happens-during-a-vacuum-extraction-delivery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Before the procedure, you’ll be informed of the risks and benefits of vacuum assistance and asked for your consent. You’ll be offered pain relief if you haven’t had it already. In some cases, your delivery assistant may need to perform an episiotomy — an incision between the birth canal and the anus — in order to widen the opening of the birth canal. They may also break your water and drain your bladder.</p>
<p>Your delivery assistant will carefully position the cup of the vacuum (ventouse) in just the right spot on your baby’s head, making sure not to trap any vaginal tissues under it. On your next contraction, they will apply traction with the mechanical or electric pump. The idea is to add the force of the vacuum to the force of your contraction, pulling when you push, and pausing when you pause.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES -
VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
38</p>
<p>The delivery assistant is trained in how to apply just the right amount of suction to the vacuum. Too much suction can cause scalp injury to the baby, but too little can cause the cup to detach from the baby’s scalp. While applying suction with one hand, they will grasp the cup with the other hand to try and guide the baby’s head through the birth canal.</p>
<p>If the cup detaches repeatedly from the baby’s head, or if there is any sign of bruising to the baby’s scalp, your delivery assistant will abandon the vacuum extractor. If the vacuum is successful, your delivery assistant will detach it as soon as your baby’s head is safely out. Now they can use their hands to help deliver the rest of the baby.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="when-should-attempted-vacuum-extraction-be-abandoned">When should attempted vacuum extraction be abandoned?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#when-should-attempted-vacuum-extraction-be-abandoned" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>When it’s been attempted for 20 minutes.</li>
<li>When the cup has detached from your baby's head multiple times.</li>
<li>When there is any sign of trauma to the baby’s scalp.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-happens-after-this-procedure">What happens after this procedure?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-happens-after-this-procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Once your baby has been completely delivered, your healthcare team will check you and your baby out for any signs of wounding from the procedure. If you had a tear or an episiotomy, they’ll repair it for you. They’ll continue to monitor your baby for any signs of complications that might arise. Some complications may take several hours to present. If no complications arise within 10 hours, you and your baby can go home and recover normally.</p>
<p>If vacuum extraction is unsuccessful, your healthcare team may recommend a c-section next.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="risks-benefits">Risks / Benefits<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risks-benefits" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="what-are-the-advantages-of-vacuum-extraction">What are the advantages of vacuum extraction?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-are-the-advantages-of-vacuum-extraction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>When conditions are favorable, vacuum extraction can help deliver your baby from an oxygen-deprived environment without putting you through surgery. It's also faster than surgery, which is sometimes very important.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="what-are-the-risks-or-complications-of-vacuum-extraction-delivery">What are the risks or complications of vacuum extraction delivery?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-are-the-risks-or-complications-of-vacuum-extraction-delivery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Risks to the mother from vacuum-assisted delivery are comparable to the risks of childbirth in general. They include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Vaginal tears.</li>
<li>Postpartum bleeding.</li>
<li>Difficulty urinating or incontinence.</li>
</ul>
<p>Short-term side effects of vacuum extraction for the baby can include:</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Caput succedaneum.</strong> Also called scalp edema, this is a swelling of the scalp that can produce a cone-headed appearance. It usually resolves in a few days.</li>
</ul>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES –
VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
39</p>
<ul>
<li>Bruising / Jaundice. The vacuum extractor can cause bruising of the scalp, which increases the risk of neonatal jaundice. This common condition produces a temporary yellowing of the baby’s skin due to increased bilirubin from the breakdown of red blood cells. It usually goes away in a few weeks.</li>
<li>Cephalohematoma. This is a collection of blood between the baby’s scalp and skull, caused by damaged blood vessels. Because the pooled blood is on the outside of the skull, it doesn’t affect the brain and is considered a minor injury. It will resolve in one or two weeks.</li>
</ul>
<p>Serious complications for the baby are rare. They can include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Skull Fracture. Newborn skulls are soft and easier to injure. Most fractures are small, heal on their own and cause no long-term damage. However, more severe fractures can cause brain bleeding, which can be damaging. Some fractures may require surgery to correct.</li>
<li>Intracranial Hemorrhage. This is bleeding either in or around the brain. Brain bleeds are rare but can be serious. Common side effects are apnea and seizures. Less commonly, the bleeding can put pressure on the brain, causing brain damage.</li>
<li>Subgaleal Hemorrhage. This occurs when the emissary veins in the baby’s head are ruptured and blood accumulates within the connective tissue between the skull and the scalp. Because of the volume of blood that can accumulate there, this condition can cause hemorrhagic shock and death if it’s not identified and treated soon enough. It usually develops gradually over the days following delivery. SGH occurs in roughly .6% of vacuum-assisted deliveries.</li>
</ul>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
40</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="vacuum-extractors">Vacuum Extractors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vacuum-extractors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-8f4735e3.jpeg" alt="img-16.jpeg"></p>
<p>A vacuum extractor, also known as a vacuum-assisted delivery, is a device used to help in moving the baby through the birth canal during delivery when a mother's labor has stalled or stopped. It is a type of assisted delivery.</p>
<p>During a vaginal delivery that has stalled for example, the baby simply hasn't moved during the past few hours a doctor will place a suction cup with a handle non baby's head to help guide her through the birth canal and into the world.</p>
<p>The vacuum extractor usually has a metal or plastic cup (flexible or semi-rigid) that is applied to the fetal vertex. Care is taken in its application to ensure that an adequate seal has been created and that no maternal soft tissue is trapped between the suction device and the fetus. Traction is then applied to the fetal head in the line of the birth canal, in an effort to assist delivery.</p>
<p>N/B: Rocking movements and torque should not be applied to the suction cup.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="needs-for-vacuum-extraction">Needs for Vacuum Extraction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#needs-for-vacuum-extraction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Vacuum extractor machine is used when;</p>
<ul>
<li>The baby is stuck in the birth canal (for example when mother is pushing, but labor is no longer progressing)</li>
<li>The mother is too tired to push</li>
</ul>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES -
VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
41</p>
<ul>
<li>The mother has a medical problem like a heart condition or very high blood pressure, both of which can make it risky to keep pushing</li>
<li>The baby is experiencing fetal distress or her heart rate indicates there's a problem</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-vacuum-extractors">Types of Vacuum Extractors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-vacuum-extractors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="i-metal-cup-vacuum-extractor">i) Metal-cup Vacuum Extractor<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#i-metal-cup-vacuum-extractor" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The metal-cup vacuum extractor has a mushroom-shaped metal cup varying from 40 to 60 mm in diameter. A centrally attached chain connects the cup to a detachable handle that is used to apply traction. A mechanical or electrical suction device is attached to the metal cup via a peripherally located vacuum port.</p>
<p>The advantages of metal-cup vacuum extraction over soft-cup extraction include a higher success rate and easier cup placement in the occipitoposterior (OP) position, especially when an OP cup is used.</p>
<p>Unfortunately, the rigidity of metal cups can make application difficult and uncomfortable, and their use is associated with an increased risk of fetal scalp injuries.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="ii-soft-cup-vacuum-extractor">ii) Soft cup Vacuum Extractor<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ii-soft-cup-vacuum-extractor" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Compared with metal-cup devices, soft-cup vacuum extractors cause fewer neonatal scalp injuries. However, these instruments have a higher failure rate.</p>
<p>Soft-cup instruments can be used with a manual vacuum pump or an electrical suction device. Some have a built-in vacuum-release valve that allows pressure to be rapidly attained and accurately controlled. This results in easy maneuverability and simplicity of operation.</p>
<p>Soft-cup vacuum extractors may be disposable or reusable.</p>
<p>Traditionally, the soft cups are bell or funnel shaped. A newer variety, the mushroom-shaped vacuum cup, or M-cup, combines the advantages of soft and metal cups.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
42</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="components-of-a-vacuum-extractor">Components of a Vacuum Extractor<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#components-of-a-vacuum-extractor" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Manual pump - Creates vacuum.</p>
<p>Vacuum gauge - Indicates the amount of pressure/vacuum used.</p>
<p>Release valve - Releases excess pressure.</p>
<p>Secretion bottle - Holds or collects unwanted fluid from the mother</p>
<p>Vacuum cup - Holds the head of the baby during delivery</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="procedure-of-performing-vacuum-extraction">Procedure of Performing Vacuum Extraction.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure-of-performing-vacuum-extraction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The woman is placed in the lithotomy position and assist throughout the process by pushing.</p>
<p>A suction cup is placed onto the head of the baby and the suction draws the skin from the scalp into the cup. Correct placement of the cup directly over the flexion point, about 3cm anterior from the occipital (posterior). It is critical to the success of the vacuum extraction.</p>
<p>Vacuum extractor has handles to allow for fraction. When the baby's head is delivered, the device is detached allowing the mother to complete the delivery of the baby.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-79965812.jpeg" alt="img-17.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="forceps-delivery-obstetrical-forceps">Forceps delivery (obstetrical forceps)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#forceps-delivery-obstetrical-forceps" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is an equipment that looks like two large spoons that the doctor inserts into the vagina and around the baby's head during a forceps delivery.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES -
VOLUME 1)</p>
<p>COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
43</p>
<p>The forceps are put into place and, the doctor uses them to gently deliver the baby’s head through the vagina. The rest of the baby is delivered normally. They were mainly being used before the invention of vacuum extractor.</p>
<p><strong>Advantages</strong> of forceps use include <strong>avoidance of caesarean section</strong> (and the short and long-term complications that accompany this), <strong>reduction of delivery time</strong>, and <strong>general applicability</strong> with cephalic presentation (head presentation).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="when-are-forceps-used">When are forceps used?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#when-are-forceps-used" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>When the baby isn’t traveling down the birth canal as expected</li>
<li>When there are concerns about the baby’s health and the doctor needs to get the baby out more quickly</li>
<li>When the mother can’t push or has been advised not to push during childbirth.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-d1b99588.jpeg" alt="img-18.jpeg">
<strong>Forcep Delivery</strong></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="risks-of-forceps-deliveries">Risks of forceps deliveries<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risks-of-forceps-deliveries" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="a-risks-on-the-baby">a) Risks on the baby<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-risks-on-the-baby" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Small facial injuries caused by the pressure of the forceps.</li>
<li>Temporary facial muscle weakness or facial palsy.</li>
<li>Skull fracture.</li>
<li>Bleeding in the skull.</li>
<li>seizures</li>
</ul>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
44</p>
<ul>
<li>Most babies do fine with a forceps delivery. Babies delivered with forceps will usually have minor marks on their faces for a short period after delivery. Serious injuries are uncommon.</li>
</ul>
<p>b) Risks on the mother</p>
<ul>
<li>Pain in the tissue between the vagina and anus after delivery</li>
<li>Tears and wounds in the lower genital tract</li>
<li>Injuries to the bladder or urethra</li>
<li>Problems with urinating or emptying the bladder</li>
<li>Short-term incontinence, or loss of bladder control</li>
<li>Anemia, or a lack of red blood cells, due to blood loss during delivery</li>
<li>Uterine rupture, or a tear in the wall of the uterus (both are extremely rare) may cause the baby or placenta to be pushed into the mother’s abdomen</li>
<li>Weakness of the muscles and ligaments that support the pelvic organs, resulting in pelvic prolapse, or the dropping of pelvic organs from their normal position</li>
</ul>
<p>Comparison of vacuum extraction to other forms of assisted delivery</p>
<p>Positive aspects</p>
<ul>
<li>An episiotomy (a surgical cut made at the opening of the vagina during childbirth to aid a difficult delivery) may not be required.</li>
<li>No special anesthesia is required.</li>
<li>The force applied to the baby can be less than that of a forceps delivery and leaves no marks on the face of the baby.</li>
<li>There is less potential for material trauma compared to forces and caesarean section.</li>
</ul>
<p>Negative aspects</p>
<ul>
<li>The baby will be left with a temporary lump (swelling) on its head.</li>
<li>There is possibly of cephalohematoma (a collection of blood between a baby’s scalp and the skull) formation.</li>
</ul>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
45</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="maintenance-of-vacuum-extractor">Maintenance of Vacuum Extractor<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maintenance-of-vacuum-extractor" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>After 4 months, service the pump and the vacuum control valve.</li>
<li>Clean the secretion bottle.</li>
<li>For electric type service the motor regularly.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="fetoscope">FETOSCOPE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fetoscope" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is a device used to obtain information about a fetus within the uterus. It is generally a special type of stethoscope known as pinard horn.</p>
<p>There are two types of fetoscopes: A fiberoptic scope for looking directly at the fetus within the uterus and a stethoscope designed for listening to the fetal heartbeat.</p>
<p>The Pinard Horn is a hollow horn-shaped stethoscope approximately 20.3cm (8") in length that is pressed against the patient's stomach. The horn must be at a precise location close to the heart in order to hear the fetal heartbeat. Because of this, it is considered to be a more accurate device than the Doppler Fetal Monitor, which picks up tones that can be further from the heart.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-d3f33ade.jpeg" alt="img-19.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-4f41f215.jpeg" alt="img-20.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="fetal-doppler">Fetal Doppler<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fetal-doppler" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is a hand held ultrasound transducer that uses sound waves to detect the heartbeat of the fetus.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES -
VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
46</p>
<p>It may be classified as a form of Doppler ultrasonography (although usually not technically - graphy but rather sound-generating).</p>
<p>It uses the Doppler effects (to provide an audible stimulation of the heartbeat).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disadvantages">Disadvantages<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is complex</p>
<p>It is expensive</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-b598cf50.jpeg" alt="img-21.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="routines-and-safety-for-vacuum-extractors">Routines and Safety for Vacuum extractors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#routines-and-safety-for-vacuum-extractors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This equipment must be kept in first-class condition.</p>
<p>After each use all parts which can be sterilized should be autoclaved. Check with the manufacturer's manual. The parts are likely to be the suction cap, the vacuum jar and the rubber tubes.</p>
<p>All parts of the machine should be kept together and numbered. They should be stored in a kit box supplied by the manufacturer or made locally, in a clean, well-ventilated area.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="daily">Daily:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#daily" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Check that a full set of the equipment is available</li>
<li>Check for visible damage to the rubber tubes, vacuum bottle or rubber plug</li>
</ol>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES -
VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
47</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Check that the vacuum release valve has a knob and washer</li>
<li>Check the traction chain for wear or damage</li>
<li>Check that the stainless steel connector tubes and gauge fit firmly into the rubber plug</li>
<li>Check that the suction caps are not damaged, especially around their rims</li>
<li>Check that the silicone bottom plates are not damaged or split</li>
<li>Check the pump and gauge for external damage</li>
</ol>
<p>Weekly (or monthly if equipment is not often used):</p>
<p>a) Check the vacuum pump:</p>
<ol>
<li>Unscrew the cap and withdraw the pump handle shaft</li>
<li>Check the main washer for wear and apply a little Vaseline. This will help produce an airtight</li>
<li>Seal between the washer and the internal pump case refit the pump handle and shaft</li>
<li>Unscrew the valve assembly cap and remove valve</li>
<li>Check the pump seal (this may be an '0' ring)</li>
<li>Check the silicone rubber membrane washer and replace if necessary (if a spare is not available, use a piece of a surgical glove)</li>
<li>Check any other washers</li>
<li>Refit valve assembly</li>
</ol>
<p>b) Check the system:
Assemble the equipment using the 40mm suction cap supplied for checking purposes. Do NOT use the cap from the clinical kit
Make sure all connections fit tightly
Apply a little Vaseline to the rubber plug
Close the screw valve
with the help of a colleague press the suction cap against your forearm and tell the colleague to pump. Check that the gauge is registering a vacuum. Check required levels with medical staff and do not exceed these when testing. Open the screw valve and release vacuum</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="infant-incubator">INFANT INCUBATOR<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#infant-incubator" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>An infant incubator is a closed chamber in which a controlled environment is provided to the premature or critically ill baby. An infant incubator is a piece of equipment common to pediatric hospitals, birthing centers and neonatal intensive care units. While the unit may serve several specific functions, it is generally used to provide a safe and stable/suitable environment for the growth of newborn infants, often those who were born prematurely or with low weight or with an illness or disability that makes them especially vulnerable for the first several months of life. The user can select the appropriate temperature, humidity and oxygen level suitable for the baby.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-228418bf.jpeg" alt="img-22.jpeg"></p>
<p>Infant incubator can include equipment to track a range of things including a baby's temperature and heart rate. This monitoring allows nurses and doctors to constantly track a baby's health status. Beyond just offering information about a baby's vitals, infant incubator will also either be open on top or have portal holes on the sides that allow it to be used in combination with various medical procedures and interventions.</p>
<p>Premature babies, also known as preemies, are those that are born before the mother has reached 37 weeks of gestation. Simply put, they are born too soon before certain key organs are</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES -
VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
49</p>
<p>able to develop. Depending on how premature the baby is, he or she may have an underdeveloped digestive tract, lungs, immune system, and even skin.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="functions-of-an-infant-incubator">Functions of an Infant Incubator<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functions-of-an-infant-incubator" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i) Protection - protects the newborn against infection and diseases and noise
ii) Feeding – Through IV and feeding tubes
iii) Administration of medication to the newborn
iv) Oxygenation – It’s achieved through head hoods, mechanical ventilation or even continuous positive airway pressure
v) Controls the humidity
vi) Controls temperature</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="basic-requirements-of-infant-incubator">Basic Requirements of Infant Incubator<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#basic-requirements-of-infant-incubator" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The most important basic requirements of infant incubators are</p>
<p><strong>Sterility</strong> - Freedom from germs (Oxygen supply filter employed)</p>
<p>Gradually adjustable temperature up to 36°C depending on the weight of the baby</p>
<p><strong>Relative humidity</strong> up to 75% or even more if desirable</p>
<p><strong>Oxygen concentration</strong> up to 40% i.e. about twice the normal Oxygen content of the atmosphere</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="operation-working-sequence-of-infant-incubator">Operation/ Working Sequence of Infant Incubator<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#operation-working-sequence-of-infant-incubator" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When the incubator is switched on, the motor is powered which in turn activates the fan. An electric fan draws room air through a bacterial filter which removes dust and bacteria. The filtered air flows over an electric heating element. The filtered and heated air then passes over a water tank where it is moistened. It then flows on to the incubator canopy. The incubator canopy is slightly pressurized. This allows expired carbon dioxide to pass back into the room via the vent holes and most of the air to be re-circulated. It also prevents unfiltered air entering the system</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)</p>
<p>COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
50</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="main-structure-and-function-of-infant-incubator">Main structure and Function of Infant Incubator<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#main-structure-and-function-of-infant-incubator" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="i-hood">i) Hood<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#i-hood" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>

<p>Functions: It's composed of 4-sided transparent windows which enables users to monitor an infant. It covers the incubators compartments and provides protection to the infant.</p>
<p>ii) Mattress
Functions: Device which is designed for placement of the infant.</p>
<p>iii) Temperature displayer
Functions: Device which enable users to monitor the temperature.</p>
<ol start="2">

Functions: Door which allows treatment of infants without opening a hood door.

Operation: Turn the handle counterclockwise, the door will close. Turn the handle clockwise, the door will open.</p>

<li>
<p>Front Door
Functions: Door designed to enable users to put infant in the incubator.
Operation: Turn the front door lock holder left or right, the door will open and pull the door down.</p>
</li>
<li>

ii) Air Flow System
Functions</p>

</ol>
<p>a) Filter
Functions: Device which is designed to supply the fresh air to hood after flitting.
If a filter is dirty, it is occupied by an infected infant.</p>
<p>iii) Fill/Drawn Water Device
Functions: Water container which supplies humidity generator with water.
Note: The water in the reservoir must be distilled water.</p>

<p>Transfusion Rack</p>

<p>b) Composition of parts Indicating Humidification Process in Modern Incubator</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="canopy-hood">Canopy (Hood):<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#canopy-hood" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the incubator cover. It's made of Perspex glass to avoid easy breakage. It's also made clear to allow for easy view of the baby inside. Easy to clean and has visible thermometer. It's significantly closed to disallow unnecessary interference from the surrounding and also keep the artificial conditions created intact.</p>
<p>This gives a confined environment to the baby. The environment is conditioned with improved temperature, humidity and Oxygen. It also protects the baby from undesirable external factors like dust and insects. It is a simulation of the mother's womb.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)</p>
