<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
53</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hand-port">Hand Port<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hand-port" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Hand Ports are for baby needs attention like turning, feeding, cleaning and manual procedures by the clinicians such as medication and emergency supply. Hands are inserted via these ports to give these services as taking the baby out of the hood or periodical opening of the hood would compromise the climate setting in the hood and expose the baby to danger.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="control-panel-unit">Control panel (unit)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#control-panel-unit" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This contains the components that set the conditions in the canopy together with their controls and alarms. The heating element, temperature controls, humidification system, sensors and alarms are all found here. Temperature setting and control knobs or buttons, visual alarm indicators and displays are on the outer plate of this device.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="electrically-operated-fan">Electrically operated Fan<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#electrically-operated-fan" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Fan located in the control box of the incubator is activated once the incubator is powered. This device is responsible for several functions including drawing in fresh atmospheric air supplies and forcing it into the canopy. It ensures uniformity of incubation conditions in the Canopy in terms of heat, Oxygen and humidity by forcing air circulation throughout the canopy. The air passes over the heating element where it gets heated and over the water bath where it warms the water to vapor. The air is then spread to all parts of the incubator canopy by the forced drought of the fan, thereby ensuring correct temperature and humidity in the canopy.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="heating-element">Heating element<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#heating-element" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Heating Element is a resistive element that gets hot when electrically powered. The level of heat is controlled using a thermostat (temperature sensor). The heat produced conditions the canopy to a temperature equivalent to that of the mother's womb which the baby needs to survive.</p>
<p>Heating element is located in the control box and heats up to a pre-set temperature; it's cut off (deactivated) by thermostatic control to keep the canopy temperature at <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>36</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">36^{\circ}\mathrm{C}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord">3</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">6</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord mathrm">C</span></span></span></span></span> as maximum. It heats up the air which circulates within the canopy by forced draft.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES -
VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT 54</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="water-reservoir-or-water-bath">Water Reservoir or Water bath<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#water-reservoir-or-water-bath" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Located in the control box, this is a small water basin that is supplied with distilled water to a specific level. The reservoir is open at the top to interact with the warm air passing over it. The water interacts at the surface with warm air forced over the heater by the fan. The water warms up and evaporates due to the warm air. The water vapor is carried in the air into the Canopy to improve humidity in the canopy</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="baby-tray">Baby Tray<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#baby-tray" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This sits at the base of the canopy. It is made of hardened plastic and holds a mackintosh-covered mattress with baby sheets. It has a tilt mechanism maneuvered from outside the canopy to change the resting angle of the baby if necessary.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="bacteria-filter">Bacteria filter<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bacteria-filter" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This traps bacteria and other pathogenic agents and keeps it out of the incubator as air is drawn into the incubator from the atmosphere. This ensures a sterile environment in the canopy where the baby stays. It gets clogged and exhausted with time and needs periodical replacement.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types-of-infant-incubators">Types of Infant Incubators<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-infant-incubators" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>There are different types of incubators that can accommodate the changing needs of the preemie. Among the five types commonly found in the NICU:</p>
<ul>
<li>Closed box incubators have a fresh air filtration system that minimizes the risk of infection and prevents the loss of moisture from the air.</li>
<li>Double-walled incubators have two walls that can further prevent heat and air moisture loss.</li>
<li>Servo-control incubators are automatically programmed to adjust temperature and humidity levels based on skin sensors attached to the baby.</li>
<li>Open box incubators, also known as Armstrong incubators, provide radiant heat below the baby but are otherwise open to the air, allowing for easy access.</li>
</ul>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)</p>
<p>COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
55</p>
<ul>
<li>Portable incubators, also known as transport incubators, are used to move the newborn from one part of the hospital to another.</li>
</ul>
<p>Discuss these different types of baby incubators.</p>
<p>N/B Incubator temperatures can vary based on the gestational age, the functional state of the baby's lungs, and other health complications.</p>
<p>Basic circuit arrangement of an infant incubator consists of: -</p>
<ul>
<li>Power source (power supply)</li>
<li>Humidity reservoir</li>
<li>Heaters (or source of heat)</li>
<li>Temperature sensor and fan</li>
<li>A means of setting and maintaining a perfect temperature for the purpose of control</li>
<li>Fan-for the purposes of oxygen and air distribution</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="temperature-control-in-infant-incubator">Temperature control in Infant Incubator<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#temperature-control-in-infant-incubator" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Simple incubators are controlled by a thermostat which consists of a sensor and a pressure can. The sensor is a thin capillary tube which leads into the pressure can (or expansion chamber). This chamber has a moveable metal lid or diaphragm. This closed system contains a liquid or gas which expands when getting warmer. The lid moves and activates a connected electrical switch.</p>
<p>The thin capillary tube is often rolled up Electronic controlled system have a cable sensor. The output controls a relay (on-off) or a dimmer (infinitely variable control).</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-80dcd4e6.jpeg" alt="img-28.jpeg"></p>
<p>The electronically controlled type has the advantage that an additional temperature sensor can be used. This sensor is taped on the skin of the baby and measures the baby's body temperature. The temperature display or thermometer should be separate from the temperature control unit. It can be a digital display or an alcohol glass thermometer.</p>
<p>N/B For safety reasons mercury thermometers must not be used in infant incubators. Mercury is toxic.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="humidity-control-in-infant-incubator">Humidity control In Infant Incubator<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#humidity-control-in-infant-incubator" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The heated air flows over the water in the water container and gets moistened. The humidity can be regulated by closing and opening a deflector plate over the container. Other incubators have a water heater which creates more humidity the warmer the water gets. The humidity should be adjustable between 40 and 90%. The humidity is measured by a hygrometer, a digital or a</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT 58</p>
<p>traditional dial instrument. The humidifier should be filled up only with distilled water only in order to avoid corrosive damage to the incubator.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="oxygen-control-in-infant-incubator">Oxygen control in Infant Incubator<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#oxygen-control-in-infant-incubator" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Most of the infant incubators have a hose connection for applying additional oxygen from an external cylinder, oxygen concentrator or from the central gas supply. In this case the warmed and moistened air gets also enriched with the oxygen. Alternatively the baby gets the additional oxygen directly via a nasal cannula.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="supplies-to-a-conventional-infant-incubator">Supplies to a conventional infant incubator<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#supplies-to-a-conventional-infant-incubator" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="heating-source-in-the-incubator">Heating source in the Incubator<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#heating-source-in-the-incubator" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="source-of-humidity">Source of humidity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#source-of-humidity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<li>Heat water (warmed H₂O)</li>
<li>The surrounding</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="humidity-distribution">Humidity Distribution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#humidity-distribution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is by convection (normal flow)</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disadvantages">Disadvantages<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It does not have even distribution</p>
<ul>
<li>Forced circulation</li>
</ul>
<p>Air drawn from out and distributed or circulated through fan</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="advantages">Advantages<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Better distribution almost even</p>
<p>It cycles air</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disadvantages">Disadvantages<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It is complicated</li>
<li>Requires additional controls (fan fail control)</li>
<li>Baby gets hot if there is no circulation (requirement of additional fan fail alarm)</li>
<li>The fan motor is supplied with single phase or split phase or low voltage motor.</li>
<li>The condition is that it must run very quietly so as not to affect the baby. Noisy motors are normally very risky to the health of the baby.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="infant-incubator-alarms">Infant Incubator Alarms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#infant-incubator-alarms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The purpose of alarm is to give warnings when predetermined conditions fail or are exceeded.</p>
<p>Types of Alarms in infant incubator are both audible and visible. They include;</p>
<ul>
<li>Power supply failure alarm</li>
<li>Air circulation/fan fail alarm</li>
<li>Heater element alarm- monitors minimum temperature</li>
<li>Over heat alarm- maximum temperature sensor</li>
<li>Circuit mal-operation alarm</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="infant-incubator-sensors">Infant-incubator Sensors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#infant-incubator-sensors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Incubator air temperature sensor
Detects the air temperature in the incubator.</p>
<p>Relative humidity sensor
Detects the temperature affected by evaporation heat. The sensor is covered with a wet nonwoven fabric.</p>
<p>Wall temperature sensor
Detects the wall temperature affected by radiation.</p>
<p>Over-temperature sensor
Detects an excessive rise in the incubator air temperature using an independent circuit.</p>
<p>Air flow sensor
Detects changes in the internal air circulation.</p>
<p>Skin temperature sensor
Detects the infant's skin temperature. The sensor is attached to the infant's skin.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nebulizer">NEBULIZER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nebulizer" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A nebulizer is a medication delivery system for aerosolized inhaled medication.</p>
<p>It changes medication from a liquid to a mist form and warms it up before the medication can be inhaled into the patient’s lungs.</p>
<p>The nebulizer works by pumping pressurized air through the liquid. Once it has formed a fine mist, the patient breathes it in through a mouthpiece or face mask. Nebulization from a drug solution is a common method of medical aerosol generation.</p>
<p>To deliver a drug by nebulization, the drug must first be dispersed in a liquid (usually aqueous) medium. After application of a dispersing force (either a jet of gas or ultrasonic waves), the drug particles are contained within the aerosol droplets, which are then inhaled.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-nebulizers">Types of Nebulizers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-nebulizers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Jet (or pneumatic) Nebulizers</li>
<li>Ultrasonic Nebulizers</li>
<li>Mesh Nebulizers</li>
</ul>
<p>In a nebulizer, the aerosol output is increased by directing auxiliary air entrained at the time of inspiration by enhanced delivery designs. Adaptive aerosol delivery monitors a patient’s breathing pattern in the first three breaths, and then targets the aerosol delivery into the first 50% of inhalation of each time. This commits that the aerosol is delivered to the patient during inspiration only, thereby eliminating loss during expiration that occurs with a continuous output nebulizer.</p>
<p>Jet nebulizers are based on the venturi principle, whereas ultrasonic nebulizers use the converse piezoelectric effect to convert alternating current to high frequency acoustic energy.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
65</p>
<p>i) Jet (Air-Jet) Nebulizers</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-0300c4ba.jpeg" alt="img-29.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-652f5856.jpeg" alt="img-30.jpeg"></p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
66</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="operation-working-principle-of-jet-nebulizer">Operation/Working Principle of Jet Nebulizer<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#operation-working-principle-of-jet-nebulizer" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The working of jet nebulizers is based on the Venturi's rule, according to which there is a decrease in the fluid pressure as it flows through a limited (narrow) sectional region.</p>
<p>A jet nebulizer unit has a T-shaped mouthpiece and a compressor employed in forcing the gas through a plastic bottle (i.e., nebulizer reservoir).</p>
<p>In these nebulizers, a jet of high-pressure airstream travels at high velocity through a narrow hole called the venturi nozzle into the drug solution which is placed in the plastic bottle. This results in the development of low pressure on the top of the drug solution. This drives the drug solution to be aerosolized up the narrow capillary tube. The small aerosol particles are inhaled by the patient through the mouthpiece and the larger droplets will hit the baffles located in various numbers and positions as per the design of the nebulizer. These impactions further atomize the bigger droplets into smaller estimated size droplets that will leave the nebulizer see figure below. In addition, baffles also regulate and reduce the velocity of aerosol releasing through the nebulizer.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-a5a9e4b9.jpeg" alt="img-31.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-ba96991b.jpeg" alt="img-32.jpeg"></p>
<p>The lowered impaction protects the oropharyngeal region of the patient during inhalation. The major issues with jet nebulizers are the compulsion for a bulky blower to produce the aerosol and the sound which get produced during the operation of the air compressor.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)</p>
<p>COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
67</p>
<p>The advantages to jet nebulization are that dose of drug alteration and dose compounding are possible. The nebulization process requires only simple and tidal breathing for drug delivery.</p>
<p>Jet nebulizers with collection bag</p>
<p>This nebulizer type releases an aerosol only during inhalation.</p>
<p>Collection bag serves up to collect and store an aerosol generated during the expiratory phase breath hold. The stored drug is further delivered to a patient in the next cycle with one-way valves that are fitted with nebulizer and located between the mouthpiece and the collection bag. In addition, Jet nebulizers with a collection bag offer an advantage in that they improve pulmonary delivery of drugs and also decrease the amount of drug loss to the environment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ii-ultrasonic-nebulizers">ii) Ultrasonic Nebulizers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ii-ultrasonic-nebulizers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Ultrasonic nebulizers are the devices that utilize a ceramic piezoelectric crystal to produce ultrasound waves, which vibrates on electrical excitation. Thus within the device chamber, high-energy waves of a specific frequency are produced in the solution. The surface waves produce small droplets that are carried away by an airstream for inhalations.</p>
<p>In addition to the piezoelectric crystal, the ultrasonic nebulizer consists of a nebulizer chamber, fan, and baffle system.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="operation-working-principle-of-ultrasonic-nebulizer">Operation/Working Principle of Ultrasonic Nebulizer<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#operation-working-principle-of-ultrasonic-nebulizer" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>During the operations of Ultrasonic Nebulizer, piezoelectric crystal owing to electric current produce vibrations of high frequency (1–3 MHz) and thus forming fountain-like structures of the drug solution. The smaller droplets are formed at the bottom of the fountain, whereas large droplets are formed at the peak of the fountain. The larger droplets are deflected by the baffles and then fragmented into smaller droplets that are then nebulized as inhalable aerosols.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-bfa1b544.jpeg" alt="img-33.jpeg"></p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES –
VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
68</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-326a5e2f.jpeg" alt="img-34.jpeg">
Figure 4: Portable ultrasonic nebulizers</p>
<p>The major features of ultrasonic nebulizer include:</p>
<ul>
<li>They generate aerosol with the higher median aerodynamic diameter and thus a coarser aerosol.</li>
<li>They offer greater output (if the parameters are optimized) than air-jet nebulizers.</li>
<li>They maintain a higher dead volume.</li>
<li>They generate a huge amount of heat within a few minutes and can increase the temperature of the drug solution by <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>20</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">20^{\circ}\mathrm{C}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord">2</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord mathrm">C</span></span></span></span></span>. This heat increases the solubility of poorly soluble drug substances.</li>
</ul>
<p>iii) Mesh Nebulizer</p>
<p>Mesh nebulizers are the newest innovation of nebulizer product to the market. They use a mesh cap with tiny holes to help dispense medication into consistent particle sizes that can be easily and comfortably inhaled.</p>
<p>Almost entirely silent, modern mesh nebulizers are also small and compact and enable complete treatment in little time possible. They are also often battery operated, giving patients the freedom to complete their respiratory treatment when they're on-the-go.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES -
VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
69</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-ea7f337a.jpeg" alt="img-35.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="conditions-treated-by-nebulizers">Conditions treated by Nebulizers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#conditions-treated-by-nebulizers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Croup. Croup is the result of one of the viruses that causes the common cold. It causes airway swelling that leads a child to develop a barking cough, runny nose, or fever.</li>
<li>Cystic fibrosis. This genetic disease can cause thick mucus to build up in the airways, clogging them and making it harder to breathe.</li>
<li>Epiglottitis. This rare condition is a result of the Haemophilus influenza, type B bacteria that can cause pneumonia. It causes severe airway swelling that leads to an abnormal, high-pitched sound when breathing.</li>
<li>Pneumonia. Pneumonia is a severe illness involving inflamed lungs. It usually requires hospitalization in babies. Symptoms include fever, shortness of breath, and changes in a baby's alertness.</li>
<li>Respiratory syncytial virus (RSV). RSV is a condition that often causes mild, cold like symptoms. While severe symptoms aren't common in older children, infants can develop inflammation of the small airways (bronchiolitis).</li>
</ul>
<p>Nebulizers can be an alternative to inhalers. These devices deliver short bursts of medication when a person inhales.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES -
VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT 70</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="repair-and-maintenance-of-nebulizers">Repair and Maintenance of Nebulizers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#repair-and-maintenance-of-nebulizers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a-jet-nebulizer">a) Jet Nebulizer<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-jet-nebulizer" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Inspect exterior of equipment for damaged or missing hardware.</li>
<li>Inspect the power cord, strain relief and plug/s for any signs of damage.</li>
<li>Turn unit off, open user accessible covers and inspect unit for damage.</li>
<li>Clean unit’s interior components and exterior with vacuum or compressed air.</li>
<li>Inspect interior for signs of corrosion or missing hardware. Repair as required.</li>
<li>Inspect electrical components for signs of excessive heat or deterioration.</li>
<li>Verify correct operation of all buttons, controls, displays and/or indicators.</li>
<li>Verify correct operation of unit in all functional modalities.</li>
<li>Clean exterior of unit including all accessories, cables, controls and displays.</li>
<li>Change air intake filter when it is gray or dirty.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="b-ultrasonic-nebulizer">b) Ultrasonic Nebulizer<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-ultrasonic-nebulizer" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Inspect exterior of equipment for damaged or missing hardware.</li>
<li>Inspect the power cord, strain relief and plug/s for any signs of damage.</li>
<li>Turn unit off, open user accessible covers and inspect unit for damage.</li>
<li>Clean unit interior components and exterior with vacuum or compressed air.</li>
<li>Inspect interior for signs of corrosion or missing hardware. Repair as required.</li>
<li>Inspect electrical components for signs of excessive heat or deterioration.</li>
<li>Inspect oxygen inlet orifice for restrictions.</li>
<li>Inspect water jet assembly including orifice. Check for water leakage.</li>
<li>Check gaskets and O-rings.</li>
<li>Verify correct ultrasonic output for sharp water cone and misting.</li>
<li>Verify correct operation of low-water cut-off circuit.</li>
<li>Tune RF output if needed.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="daily-cleaning-of-nebulizers">Daily cleaning of Nebulizers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#daily-cleaning-of-nebulizers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Take off the mouthpiece/mask and remove the medicine container. Wash this with hot water and mild liquid dish soap.</li>
</ul>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)</p>
<p>COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT 71</p>
<ul>
<li>Shake off the extra water.</li>
<li>Reconnect the medicine container and mouthpiece/mask to the compressor. Turn on the device to air dry the pieces.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disinfecting-nebulizers">Disinfecting Nebulizers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disinfecting-nebulizers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Take off the detachable parts (mouthpiece and medicine container).</li>
<li>Soak them in the solution of one part white vinegar and three parts hot water.</li>
<li>Let these parts soak for one hour, or as long as listed on the instructions.</li>
<li>Remove the parts and either let them air dry or reconnect the machine to dry them.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="advantages-of-nebulizers">Advantages of Nebulizers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages-of-nebulizers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>They are easier to use when one has an asthma attack, since he/she doesn't need to take deep breaths while using one.</li>
<li>Multiple medications can be delivered at the same time.</li>
<li>A nebulizer may be easier to use with young children.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disadvantages-of-nebulizers">Disadvantages of Nebulizers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantages-of-nebulizers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Nebulizers are usually not as easy to transport as an inhaler.</li>
<li>They often require a stationary power source.</li>
<li>Delivery of medications takes longer through a nebulizer than through an inhaler.</li>
</ul>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)</p>
<p>COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT 72</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="radiant-warmer">RADIANT WARMER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#radiant-warmer" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-948d3e81.jpeg" alt="img-36.jpeg">
Main Structure</p>
<p>Radiant warmers are equipment’s which provide radiating heat to minimize energy requirements for heat production, decreasing the risks of low blood sugar and increased work of breathing associated with hypothermia.</p>
<p>They provide an area where resuscitations, procedures, and short-term observation can take place while keeping the baby warm. Warmers may vary in complexity, including only heating functionality or heating functionality with resuscitation and oxygen equipment. All warmers include a temperature probe that provides information on the patient’s temperature.</p>
<p>Radiant warmers may be used both within the Nursery ward and the Labor or Obstetrics ward. Warmers are used exclusively for newborn or young pediatrics patients.</p>
<p>Radiant warmers may be used on all neonatal patients admitted to the nursery ward, but especially for those with prematurity, low birth weight, reduced growth, low body temperature or undergoing procedures.</p>
<p>N/B: Newborn babies can drop their body temperature very quickly, even within minutes. They must be kept warm from the moment of birth, during their time in the labor ward and when transferred to the nursery. Even small drops in temperature increase the likelihood of mortality.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mechanisms-of-heat-loss-in-babies">Mechanisms of Heat Loss in Babies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mechanisms-of-heat-loss-in-babies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Newborn babies lose heat through four main mechanisms</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)</p>
<p>COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
73</p>
<ul>
<li>Evaporation: water loss through the skin.</li>
<li>Radiation: heat radiating from the warmer patient towards cooler surfaces (e.g., windows or walls).</li>
<li>Conduction: direct heat travelling from warmer surface of the skin to the cooler mat or cot on which the patient rests.</li>
<li>Convection: air currents move heat away from the skin/body.</li>
</ul>
<p>N/B: Norm thermic axillary temperature in neonates ranges from 36.5°C to 37.5°C. Every effort must be made to keep a baby's temperature within the normal range as temperature below 36°C is an independent risk factor for death in newborns.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-8d503e81.jpeg" alt="img-37.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="working-operation-of-radiant-warmer">Working/Operation of Radiant Warmer<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#working-operation-of-radiant-warmer" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A radiant warmer consists of a mounted overhead heating mechanism that may be transported or kept stationary with lockable castors. This heating mechanism consists of heating elements (typically made of ceramic or quartz). In both types of heating elements, an optically designed parabolic reflector is fitted into the heating element housing to direct the heat energy towards the baby cot.</p>
<p>The baby cot may be part of the radiant warmer or the heating elements may be independent (as in phototherapy lights). Heat output from the heating elements is controlled by the main controller which in turn is dictated by user input. In some units, a separate module is fitted to control the heater output.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
74</p>
<p>The core temperature of the baby is continuously monitored by the <strong>temperature probe</strong> connected to the device and placed over the baby’s liver. Body temperature changes can be seen in real-time on a small LCD panel. Radiant warmers are also fitted with <strong>audiovisual alarms</strong> to attract the attention of the medical or technical staff when a problem occurs.</p>
<p><strong>N/B</strong>: Radiant warmers heat in various modes i.e.</p>
<p><strong>Pre-warm Mode</strong>: provides constant low heat for a short amount of time (typically 10 minutes or less) to warm the cot underneath the warmer. Pre-warming protects the patient from conductive heat loss caused by a cold mattress.</p>
<p><strong>Automatic Mode</strong>: also called <strong>servo</strong> or <strong>baby mode</strong>; uses a temperature probe on the baby to automatically adjust heat provided to maintain the patient’s temperature within an acceptable range.</p>
<p><strong>Manual Mode</strong>: provides a constant, unadjusting heat that is set by the user. Patients should never be left unattended if being treated in manual mode.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="main-components-of-radiant-warmer">Main Components of Radiant Warmer<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#main-components-of-radiant-warmer" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="power-switch">Power switch<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#power-switch" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The power switch is usually a rocker switch located on the back or side of the unit. This switch must be in the “on” position to power the radiant warmer and view the control panel.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="control-panel">Control Panel<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#control-panel" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>A control panel, usually located on the front of the radiant warmer, includes functions for operating the radiant warmer and a display of readings to assist in clinical care. Most control panels include:</p>
<ul>
<li>An LCD that displays readings from the temperature probe, the set temperature for the warmer, the heat power output, fault codes, alarms, and other status readings based on the manufacture’s design.</li>
<li>Some models will have an LCD touchscreen that includes controls for the radiant warmer, (i.e., exam lights, alarms, timers, and temperature adjustments).</li>
</ul>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
75</p>
<ul>
<li>Radiant warmer controls either will be located on the LCD touchscreen or will be physical buttons, knobs, or switches on the warmer. These controls will be used to adjust the temperature, set temperature input, and select the warming mode.</li>
<li>Some radiant warmer control panels will maintain settings from the last use. For this reason, always advise the clinical or nursing staff to check the settings.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="patient-temperature-probe">Patient Temperature Probe<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#patient-temperature-probe" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The manufacturer includes a patient temperature probe cable that is designed to be used with their radiant warmer model. The patient temperature sensor end of the cable is intended to be placed on the baby’s skin over the liver to read the body temperature.</p>
<p>This end is typically made of a thermocouple that measures and feeds the patient’s temperature back to the control PCB’s microcontroller. The microcontroller uses the patient’s temperature readings to provide feedback to the control system, which will adjust the heater output based on the comparison between the actual baby core temperature measured by the probe and the user set value (as in servo/automatic mode) or to turn off the heater (as in manual mode).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="patient-temperature-probe-port">Patient Temperature Probe Port<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#patient-temperature-probe-port" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The patient temperature probe port on the unit is designed to fit the manufacture’s specified patient temperature probe cable. The port end of the cable is inserted into the port. This cable links the control system and the patient temperature probe to provide the patient’s temperature readings the PCB microcontroller.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="baby-cot">Baby Cot<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#baby-cot" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Some radiant warmers include an attached baby cot. The cot often includes removable side panels that should be in place and secure when the baby is in the cot to prevent falls. The cot may also include a knob underneath the cot to adjust the position of the cot.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="power-supply-unit-psu">Power Supply Unit (PSU)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#power-supply-unit-psu" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Linear power supply</li>
</ul>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
76</p>
<p>Its main function is to convert 110/220 VAC mains power to low voltage regulated DC power for use in other electronic circuits in the system as per design. The basic components of power supply unit are transformer, rectifiers, Voltage regulators, and filters.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-5728724b.jpeg" alt="img-38.jpeg"></p>
<ul>
<li>Switch mode power supply</li>
</ul>
<p>It's common in modern phototherapy units and radiant warmers. They use semiconductor (MOSFETS) switching techniques to convert AC to DC. Their main advantages are that they are compact, reduced heat dissipation and they consume less power.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-c9eaad5a.jpeg" alt="img-39.jpeg"></p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES -
VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
77</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="control-pcb">Control PCB<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#control-pcb" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The control PCB includes the microcontroller and regulates all the system operations and electronic circuits. All auxiliary control units, if fitted, report to the main control PCB. The control system's microcontroller performs regular self-tests during operation. Whenever the system detects an issue with the temperature control system or working state, the device will issue a corresponding visual or audio alarm.</p>
<p>The LCD, the heater output, alarms, and monitoring of system operations is controlled through the control PCB. Comparator circuits on the control PCB compare the signal from temperature probes and the set temperature value (as in servo/automatic mode). It uses this input to control the heater output using relays (either solid state or electromechanical) which switch the heating element on/off to maintain the set temperature.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="heating-elements">Heating Elements<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#heating-elements" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>There are two main types of heating elements used in radiant warmers: ceramic and quartz. They are usually between 800 W or 1000 W, and they release radiant heat in the far infrared wavelength that is easily absorbed by the neonate's body.</p>
<ul>
<li>Ceramic heating elements use a heating wire (e.g., nichrome) encapsulated in a ceramic material. When power is applied the ceramic plate is warmed and radiates heat to the baby cot.</li>
<li>Quartz heating elements consist of a coiled heating element enclosed in a quartz tube. When electricity is applied, the quartz warms, and radiates heat to the baby cot.</li>
</ul>
<p>Both ceramic and quartz elements use an optically designed parabolic reflector that is fitted to project heat energy onto to the baby cot.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="internal-battery">Internal Battery<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#internal-battery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The internal battery operates alarms during power failure.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="audiovisual-alarms">Audiovisual Alarms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#audiovisual-alarms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The control PCB's microcontroller performs regular self-tests during operation. Whenever the system detects an issue with the temperature control system or working state, the device will issue a corresponding visual and/or audio alarm or error code. The common alarms found on radiant warmers are:</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES -
VOLUME 1)</p>
<p>COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
78</p>
<ul>
<li>Temperature Alarm: works only in servo/automatic mode. It activates when the baby's temperature (measured by the patient temperature probe) deviates from the user set temperature by <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>±</mo><msup><mn>1</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\pm 1^{\circ}\mathrm{C}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7667em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">±</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">1</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord mathrm">C</span></span></span></span></span>. A visual alarm flashes and is followed by an audible alarm.</li>
<li>Probe Failure Alarm: works only in servo/automatic mode. It activates when the probe fails electronically, or when the probe is disconnected from the warmer. During a probe failure, the heater deactivates, a visual alarm flashes followed by an audio alarm. The LCD will show an error code.</li>
<li>System Failure Alarm: activates when the systems fail or calibration deviates from expected values.</li>
<li>Heater Failure Alarm: activates when a heater defect is detected. An error code is displayed on the LCD.</li>
<li>Power Failure: activates when a power failure is detected. Battery power supports this audible alarm during power outages.</li>
</ul>
<p>Manufacturers may include different alarms and error codes based on the model.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="firmware">Firmware<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#firmware" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Radiant warmer firmware controls display and functionality for the radiant warmer. It is defined by the manufacturer and may be used to update the radiant warmer to display specific parameters or respond in a set way.</p>
<p>Firmware is the software that carries out the basic functions of the radiant warmer. This software is stored in the memory within the radiant warmer's hardware. The manufacturer may issue occasional updates to the firmware that will need to be applied to existing radiant warmers per the manufacturer's instructions.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications-related-with-a-baby-warmer">Complications related with a baby warmer<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications-related-with-a-baby-warmer" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Introduction of equipment in newborn care units poses clinical and device complications for patients. Awareness of potential complications is critical to maximize patient safety.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
79</p>
<p>i) Clinical complications</p>
<p>Hypothermia &amp; cold stress: if the device is not prepared correctly, is malfunctioning, or the baby is left exposed for a long period of time, there is a risk of hypothermia. This is associated with a significant increase in mortality and morbidity.</p>
<p>Hyperthermia &amp; heat stress: hyperthermia can occur in patients whilst on manual mode who are not monitored regularly or on servo mode if the temperature probe falls off as they may become overheated. Hyperthermia increases morbidity and mortality.</p>
<p>Pressure sores: pressure sores may develop if the patient is incorrectly positioned is lying on additional tubing/equipment, or the temperature probe is not positioned correctly.</p>
<p>Falls: the cot sides of the radiant warmer must be in place to prevent the baby falling off the mattress on to the floor.</p>
<p>Infection: if the temperature probe or infant warmer are not cleaned thoroughly before use, infection can be transmitted. Care should be taken particularly for consumables that are marked as single-use but are reused in practice (such as temperature probes).</p>
<p>ii) Device Complications</p>
<p>Hyperthermia due to probe mismanagement: if the device is set to automatically adjust its temperature based on the patient's temperature (servo mode) and the patient temperature probe falls off the patient or is not well secured, the radiant warmer may overheat in an attempt to compensate for what it observes as a low body temperature. This puts the patient at risk for a body temperature &gt; 40 degrees Celsius and clinical harm.</p>
<p>Alarms: radiant warmers have in-built alarms that should sound if the patient's temperature is above or below a set norm thermic range. If this range is not appropriately set, alarms may sound inappropriately.</p>
<p>Fire: if linen is placed on the radiant heater head, heat and dust may build up and pose a fire hazard. Linen should never be stored on top of the device or close to the heating elements. Although treatment devices (e.g., phototherapy units, oxygen concentrators) can be used with a</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES -
VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
80</p>
<p>radiant warmer, care should be taken to ensure that the direct line of heat to the patient from the radiant warmer heating elements is not obstructed.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preventive-maintenance-of-radiant-warmer">Preventive Maintenance of Radiant Warmer<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preventive-maintenance-of-radiant-warmer" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="i-after-each-use">i) After Each Use<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#i-after-each-use" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Turn off and unplug the radiant warmer. Allow to cool. Use gauze and 70% alcohol to thoroughly wipe: Temperature probe, including cable and plug head,</p>
<p>Control panel, Power button, Mattress, Bassinet walls &amp; floor.</p>
<p>Visually inspect radiant warmer components.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="ii-weekly-maintenance">ii) Weekly Maintenance<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ii-weekly-maintenance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Test the heating elements and temperature probe:</p>
<ul>
<li>Plug in the machine. Connect the temperature probe. Turn the power switch to ON. Leave the machine on for 1 minute.</li>
<li>Hold the temperature probe in the palm of your hand and hold your hand near the overhead heating elements. Slowly move it from the part of the heating element closest to the stand, moving towards the outside end of the heating element. You should feel your hand progressively heat as it moves and see the temperature reading on the machine steadily increase.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="iii-monthly-maintenance">iii) Monthly Maintenance<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#iii-monthly-maintenance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Perform Weekly preventive maintenance steps.</li>
<li>Test the power loss alarm: while the radiant warmer is plugged in and turned on, turn off the power at the wall socket. An alarm should sound.</li>
<li>Check the castors for proper movement and brake functions.</li>
<li>Check the operation of the baby cot, tilting mechanism and drawers.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="iv-quarterly-maintenance">iv) Quarterly Maintenance<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#iv-quarterly-maintenance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>

<li>Perform Monthly preventive maintenance steps.</li>
