<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="phototherapy-machine-photobox">PHOTOTHERAPY MACHINE (PHOTOBOX)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#phototherapy-machine-photobox" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Phototherapy lights from the phototherapy machine or unit is used exclusively within the newborn care ward for newborn patients that display symptoms of jaundice or hyper bilirubinemia (high bilirubin levels).</p>
<p>Jaundice is a yellow discoloration of a newborn baby’s skin and eyes and it occurs because the baby’s blood contains excess bilirubin (a yellow pigment of red blood cells).</p>
<p>Infant jaundice is a common condition particularly in babies born before 38 weeks of gestation (preterm babies) and some breastfeeding babies.</p>
<p>It usually occurs when the baby’s liver is not mature enough to get rid of excess bilirubin in the blood stream.</p>
<p>Phototherapy may be considered for neonates with jaundice based on the age at which they show symptoms, measured blood or skin bilirubin concentrations or with specific complications with which they present.</p>
<p>Phototherapy uses blue light transmitted on the patient’s skin within the wavelengths of 425 to 475 nm to break down unconjugated bilirubin to a water-soluble, non-toxic form that can be easily excreted. Phototherapy lights may be integrated into units with overhead, over- and under-body, or flexible blanket lights.</p>
<p>Most phototherapy units can be used in tandem with other devices (e.g., radiant warmers, incubators, and oxygen therapy).</p>
<p>Phototherapy lights are most effective when providing blue-green light within 425 to 475 nm via LEDs. Other types of bulbs providing blue light within 425 to 475 nm (e.g., halogen or fluorescent) are less effective for treating jaundice, have a shorter lifetime, and are not as sustainable for long term use.</p>
<p>Halogen and fluorescent bulbs are less efficient than LEDs and may also be a source of heat, introducing a potential risk for hyperthermia.</p>
<p>Other types of phototherapy are also used, but are typically not recommended:</p>
<ul>
<li>UV lights: not recommended for neonatal therapy due to increased melanoma risk associated with childhood UV exposure.</li>
</ul>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
84</p>
<ul>
<li>Natural sunlight: traditionally used in lieu of phototherapy devices; natural sunlight is not ideal due to increased challenges with temperature control of the patient and UV radiation risks.</li>
<li>Filtered sunlight: there is emerging evidence that devices that filter sunlight, while requiring close monitoring in order to prevent temperature instability, can be used in babies &gt; 2.2kg in tropical climates to treat neonatal jaundice.</li>
</ul>
<p>N/B: Most jaundiced patients require treatment for 24 to 48 hours, and typically do not require treatment for any longer than seven days. If jaundice persists, further investigation into the cause of the jaundice should be advised.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="operation-working-of-phototherapy-unit">Operation/Working of Phototherapy Unit<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#operation-working-of-phototherapy-unit" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Phototherapy Unit has a lamp that emits a spectral irradiance (µW/cm²/nm), which is optimized when the light source is set to the recommended distance (height) from the patient.</p>
<p>Phototherapy lights' output is controlled in various modes i.e. Standard mode which provides usual optimal spectral irradiance for conventional phototherapy (25-30 µW/cm²/nm) and Intensive mode that provides higher optimal spectral irradiances for intensive phototherapy (30-35 µW/cm²/nm).</p>
<p>N/B: Phototherapy lights are not heaters. Any heat provided by the phototherapy light is minimal and due to the efficiency of the lighting assemblies within the unit. This heat emission is not typically strong enough to provide sufficient heat to prevent a neonatal patient from becoming hypothermic. Although similar to radiant warmers in design, the purpose of the phototherapy light is solely to provide therapeutic light (blue-green) to treat jaundice.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-86866437.jpeg" alt="img-40.jpeg"></p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES -
VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
85</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="device-flow-diagram">Device Flow Diagram<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#device-flow-diagram" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-e48b66f2.jpeg" alt="img-41.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="main-components-of-the-phototherapy-unit">Main Components of the Phototherapy Unit<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#main-components-of-the-phototherapy-unit" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>On/Off Button</li>
</ul>
<p>The On/Off button powers on and off phototherapy units by a button located on the control panel or at the back of the unit.</p>
<ul>
<li>Control Panel</li>
</ul>
<p>The control panel, located in the front of the phototherapy light, includes an LCD that usually displays treatment time and mode.</p>
<p>Some models may show intensity value indicators and total device hours (the total number of hours the light has been used).</p>
<p>The control panel also houses buttons to control the settings, such as:</p>
<p>i) Intensity selection keys
ii) On/off switch
iii) Observation light switch</p>
<ul>
<li>Power Supply Unit (PSU)</li>
</ul>
<p>The PSU is located internally within the phototherapy light. Its main function is to convert AC mains power (110 or 220 V) to lower voltage regulated DC power (typically 24 V).</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES -
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO
VOLUME 1)</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
86</p>
<p>The basic components within a power supply are a transformer, rectifier, voltage regulator and filters.</p>
<p>Switch mode power supplies (SMPS) are common in modern phototherapy units. They use semiconductor (MOSFETS) switching techniques to convert AC to DC. Their main advantages are that they are compact, have reduced heat dissipation and they consume less power.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-ddd1622d.jpeg" alt="img-42.jpeg"></p>
<ul>
<li>Control PCB</li>
</ul>
<p>The control PCB executes all operations of the machine, controls the display, interfaces with the input keys, controls the LEDs' intensity, and sets the timer. It also monitors the system and collects errors for diagnosis and troubleshooting.</p>
<ul>
<li>Lighting panel</li>
</ul>
<p>The lighting panel is mounted internally and houses light bulb or LED assemblies. These may be connected in series or parallel depending on the model.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES –
VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
87</p>
<p>The lighting panel emits blue-green light of (425 to 475 nm) which is the appropriate wavelength to break down excess bilirubin in the bloodstream.</p>
<ul>
<li>Light meter</li>
</ul>
<p>The light meter may be a separate measurement device or attached to phototherapy light. The light meter is typically a simple device, with a digital readout and photo sensor to measure effective 425 to 475 nm irradiance delivered in <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>μ</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">W</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><msup><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">c</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi></mrow><mn>2</mn></msup><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">n</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mu \mathrm{W} / \mathrm{cm}^2/\mathrm{nm}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.0641em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">μ</span><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right: 0.01389em;">W</span><span class="mord">/</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">cm</span></span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8141em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">2</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord">/</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">nm</span></span></span></span></span></span>.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="setting-up-the-machine-for-a-patient">Setting up the Machine for a Patient<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#setting-up-the-machine-for-a-patient" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Collect:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Phototherapy device</li>
<li>Power cable</li>
<li>Phototherapy light meter (if available)</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>
<p>Plug in phototherapy device. Turn on and check for blue-green light from the overhead light elements. Some phototherapy lights may have white examination lights. In most models, if light emitting from this type of device is white, it is not therapeutic.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Turn on light meter if available. Place light meter on the mattress where the patient needing phototherapy will be located.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The phototherapy unit is typically set at a point where the overhead lights are approximately 20 - 30 cm above a typical cot. Light should cover the entire surface on which the patient will be treated. Check that irradiance provided at this height is within therapeutic ranges and adjust height if necessary.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>If irradiance is too low, lower the height of the light until therapeutic ranges are reached without obstructing care.</li>
<li>If irradiance is too high, raise the height of the light until therapeutic ranges are reached.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-complications-of-the-patient">Clinical Complications of the Patient<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-complications-of-the-patient" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Dehydration: neonatal patients under phototherapy with lights other than LEDs may require more fluid than maintenance volumes.</li>
</ul>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES -
VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
88</p>
<ul>
<li>Hypothermia: temperature should be carefully monitored as patients are nearly naked under phototherapy. LED bulbs used in modern devices are very efficient and generate minimal heat; thermal support may be required to avoid hypothermia.</li>
<li>Retinal damage: consistent exposure of the eyes to strong light has been shown to cause retinal damage in adults. Although this has not been tested in neonates, care should be taken to keep the eyes covered at all times during treatment.</li>
<li>Eye infections: check for redness, swelling or discharge. The skin under the eye pads should be cleaned daily with warm sterile water to prevent infection.</li>
<li>Bronze baby syndrome: some babies develop a greyish color to their skin, urine, and plasma during phototherapy. This is self-limiting and resolves after phototherapy is stopped.</li>
</ul>
<p>Acute bilirubin encephalopathy (Kernicterus): if phototherapy settings are too low or the light is nearing the end of its bulb lifetime, bilirubin may not be effectively broken down during treatment. Extremely high levels of bilirubin can cross the blood brain barrier and cause permanent brain damage. In addition to phototherapy, exchange blood transfusions are required for serious jaundice.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="device-complications">Device Complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#device-complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Inadequate light: after a set period of use (20,000 – 50,000 hours, depending on manufacturer recommendations), phototherapy devices may lose their ability to provide therapeutic light.</p>
<p>It is important to test the capacity of the phototherapy regularly to ensure that the phototherapy light is still providing a therapeutic range (25 – 35 µW/cm²).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preventive-maintenance-of-phototherapy-machine">Preventive Maintenance of phototherapy machine<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preventive-maintenance-of-phototherapy-machine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i) After Each Use (Daily)</p>
<p>Turn off and unplug the phototherapy light. Use gauze and 70% alcohol or diluted chlorine to thoroughly wipe:</p>
<ul>
<li>Phototherapy light meter, including cable and plug head if applicable.</li>
<li>Control panel</li>
<li>Power button</li>
</ul>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)</p>
<p>COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
89</p>
<p>Visually inspect phototherapy light components.</p>
<p>ii) Monthly</p>
<p>Test the therapeutic irradiance of the phototherapy light:</p>
<ul>
<li>Plug in the machine. Connect the temperature probe. Turn the power switch to ON. Leave the machine on for 1 minute.</li>
<li>Plug in phototherapy device. Turn on and check for blue-green light from the overhead light elements. NOTE: Some phototherapy lights may have white examination lights. In most models, if light emitting from this type of device is white, it is not therapeutic.</li>
<li>Turn on light meter if available. Place light meter on the mattress where the patient needing phototherapy will be located.</li>
<li>Read the irradiance measurement at 40 cm</li>
</ul>
<p>Check the castors for proper movement and brake functions.</p>
<p>Document cumulative hours run and preventive maintenance actions taken.</p>
<p>Troubleshooting &amp; Repair</p>
