<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="resuscitaire-unit">RESUSCITAIRE UNIT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#resuscitaire-unit" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Features of the Resuscitaire Radiant Warmer (RW82)</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-35352e1b.jpeg" alt="img-43.jpeg"></p>
<p>A resuscitaire is a medical device used by midwives and other health care professionals when the baby requires some additional support with their breathing after birth.</p>
<p>In some cases, it is used for clinical emergencies such as resuscitation. This is when the baby requires much more support than just facial oxygen.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="why-do-some-babies-need-help-in-taking-their-first-breaths-when-born">Why do some babies need help in taking their first breaths when born?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#why-do-some-babies-need-help-in-taking-their-first-breaths-when-born" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When the baby is in the womb, their lungs are filled with fluid as they don't need to use lungs for breathing. They get everything they need from the placenta via their umbilical cord.</p>
<p>When they are born and the cord is cut, they need to breathe for themselves. The fluid in their lungs is pushed out and when they take their first breaths (and big cries), air and oxygen inflates their lungs thus breathing normally. Most babies need very little stimulation to help them to do this. So the baby resuscitaire is an ideal device to help a midwife or other healthcare professional to assist the baby.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES –
VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
92</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="working-principle">Working Principle<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#working-principle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A resuscitaire creates a controlled environment to give intensive care to new-born children who may experience some difficulties. e. g. the baby may not breathe well, maybe due to inadequate oxygenation of the mother’s blood or inadequate blood flow during anesthesia.</p>
<p>The baby resuscitaire has an overhead heater which that facilitates warming of the baby. The device has a small face mask to help a midwife or healthcare professional give the baby some facial oxygen. This helps the baby take their inflation breaths to expand their lungs and get rid of any fluid that might need to be released.</p>
<p>There’s also a drawer that contains all baby equipment.</p>
<p>Environmental factors that are controlled by the resuscitaire include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Temperature</li>
<li>Humidity</li>
<li>Oxygen</li>
<li>Light</li>
</ul>
<p>In addition, the unit includes medical equipment for immediate use such as: suction unit, ventilator, gas flow meter.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="functions">Functions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="i-thermo-regulation">i) Thermo-regulation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#i-thermo-regulation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>To regulate body temperature, most resuscitaires use a Radiant warmer / heater, combined with an insulating mattress.</p>
<p>The heater is positioned approximately 1 meter above the level of the infant, reflecting heat downwards. The warmer has a pre-warm mode, a Manual mode or a Baby mode.</p>
<p>In the Baby mode, the unit uses a temperature sensor which needs to be connected to the baby (at the location of the liver, which usually has good blood flow). The system allows the user to set a temperature range. This range is then automatically maintained by the system. In manual mode, which needs to be used if the temperature sensor is broken or lost, the heater will operate</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
93</p>
<p>in manual mode, with constant output. This mode is more dangerous as the baby can be overheated. A warmer head pivot can be present to rotate the warmer to the side to enable X-ray.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ii-ventilation">ii) Ventilation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ii-ventilation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The ventilator needs to make sure that the air pressure is as low as possible to get a given volume of air/oxygen into the lungs.</p>
<p>The baby’s lung compliance changes continuously. The ventilator pressure must be adapted to take this into account.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="iii-lighting">iii) Lighting<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#iii-lighting" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Resuscitaires (and infant warmers) have exam lights built into the warming hoods. The exam lights can vary from simple incandescent light bulbs, to mini-spot lights to reflector type (Halogen) lamps.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="main-parts-of-a-resuscitaire">Main parts of a Resuscitaire<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#main-parts-of-a-resuscitaire" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i) Controller (Control panel)
ii) Blender gas supply module
iii) Gas supply module
iv) Resuscitation module
v) Warmer head
vi) Bassinet
vii) Mattress/cot
viii) Resuscitation and suction equipment storage compartment
ix) Handle</p>
<p>Control panel is the main interface of the machine where the operator can adjust the settings and monitor the baby’s vital signs.</p>
<p>Gas supply module (Oxygen source) provides the oxygen supply to the machine which is essential for resuscitation.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT 94</p>
<p>Ventilation Unit (blender gas supply module) delivers positive pressure ventilation to the baby's lungs to help the baby breath.</p>
<p>Temperature control Unit (warmer head) maintains the baby's body temperature which is critical for their survival.</p>
<p>Monitoring Unit displays the baby's body vital signs such as heart rate, oxygen saturation and respiratory rates.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="inputs-and-outputs-of-a-resuscitaire">Inputs and outputs of a Resuscitaire<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#inputs-and-outputs-of-a-resuscitaire" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="inputs">Inputs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#inputs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Power</li>
<li>Oxygen</li>
<li>Air</li>
<li>Water</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="outputs">Outputs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#outputs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Oxygen under pressure for ventilation</li>
<li>Heat for warming the baby (temperature control)</li>
<li>Suctions</li>
<li>Alarms</li>
<li>Light</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="common-faults-and-remedies-of-a-resuscitaire">Common faults and Remedies of a Resuscitaire<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-faults-and-remedies-of-a-resuscitaire" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="oxygen-supply-issues">Oxygen supply issues<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#oxygen-supply-issues" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>If there is an issue with oxygen supply, the blender may not be able to deliver the correct amount of oxygen at the required pressure to the baby.</p>
<p>This can be corrected by checking the oxygen source and making sure it's connected properly.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)</p>
<p>COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT 95</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="suction-system-blockage">Suction System blockage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#suction-system-blockage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>If the suction system is blocked, it may not be able to clear the baby’s airway effectively. This can be remedied by checking the suction catheter for blockage and clearing them if necessary.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="malfunctioning-warmers">Malfunctioning warmers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#malfunctioning-warmers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>If the warmer is not functioning correctly, it may not be able to maintain the baby’s body temperature.</p>
<p>This can be corrected by checking the temperature sensor and making sure it’s working or functioning properly.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="phototherapy-unit-having-issues">Phototherapy unit having issues<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#phototherapy-unit-having-issues" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>If the phototherapy is not working correctly, it may not be able to treat jaundice effectively.</p>
<p>This can be remedied by checking the light source and making sure it is functioning properly.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="maintenance-and-repair-of-a-resuscitaire">Maintenance and Repair of a Resuscitaire<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maintenance-and-repair-of-a-resuscitaire" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i) Check the oxygen supply and make sure it is connected properly
ii) Check the suction catheter for blockage and clearing them if necessary
iii) Check the temperature sensor and ensure its functioning properly
iv) Check the light source of the phototherapy unit and examination light making sure that they function properly.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)</p>
<p>COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
96</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="fetal-monitor">FETAL MONITOR<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fetal-monitor" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is a device used to evaluate the well-being of the fetus by assessing the rate and rhythm of the fetal heartbeat.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="methods-of-fetal-heart-rate-monitoring">Methods of fetal heart rate monitoring<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#methods-of-fetal-heart-rate-monitoring" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are two methods for fetal heart rate monitoring, external and internal;</p>
<p>External fetal heart rate monitoring uses a device to listen to or record the fetal heartbeat through the mother's abdomen.</p>
<p>A fetoscope (a type of stethoscope) is the most basic type of external monitor. Another type of monitor is a hand-held electronic Doppler ultrasound device.</p>
<p>A fetoscope or Doppler device may also be used to check the fetal heart rate at regular intervals during labor. Continuous electronic fetal heart monitoring may be used during labor and birth.</p>
<p>An ultrasound transducer placed on the mother's abdomen conducts the sounds of the fetal heart to a computer. The rate and pattern of the fetal heart are displayed on the computer screen and printed onto special graph paper.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-9262a9ef.jpeg" alt="img-44.jpeg"></p>
<p>Internal fetal heart rate monitoring uses an electronic transducer connected directly to the fetal skin. A wire electrode is attached to the fetal scalp or other body part through the cervical opening and is connected to the monitor. This type of electrode is sometimes called a spiral or scalp electrode.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES -
VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
97</p>
<p>Internal monitoring provides a more accurate and consistent transmission of the fetal heart rate than external monitoring because factors such as movement do not affect it.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="need-for-fetal-heart-monitoring">Need for fetal heart monitoring<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#need-for-fetal-heart-monitoring" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Fetal heart rate monitoring is especially helpful when one has a high-risk pregnancy. The pregnancy is of a high risk when one has diabetes or high blood pressure.</li>
<li>Fetal heart rate monitoring may be used to check how preterm <strong>labor medicines</strong> (medicines used to help keep labor from starting too early) are affecting the baby in the womb.</li>
</ul>
<p>Fetal heart rate monitoring may be used in other tests which include;</p>
<p>i) Non-stress test. This measures the fetal heart rate as the baby moves.
ii) Contraction stress test. It measures fetal heart rate along with uterine contractions. Contractions are started with medicine or other methods.
iii) A biophysical profile (BPP). This test combines a non-stress test with ultrasound.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="things-that-may-affect-the-fetal-heart-rate-during-labor">Things that may affect the fetal heart rate during labor<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#things-that-may-affect-the-fetal-heart-rate-during-labor" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Uterine contractions</li>
<li>Pain-reliever medicines or anesthesia given to the mother during labor</li>
<li>Tests done during labor</li>
<li>Pushing during the second stage of labor</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="contributors-to-less-accurate-fetal-heart-rate-monitoring">Contributors to less accurate fetal heart rate monitoring<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contributors-to-less-accurate-fetal-heart-rate-monitoring" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Obesity of the mother</li>
<li>Position of the baby or mother</li>
<li>Too much amniotic fluid (poly-hydramnios)</li>
<li>Cervix is not dilated or the amniotic sac is not broken. Both of these need to happen for internal monitoring.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="risks-of-fetal-heart-monitoring">Risks of fetal heart monitoring<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risks-of-fetal-heart-monitoring" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Risks of internal monitoring include <strong>infection and bruising</strong> of the baby’s scalp or other body parts.</li>
</ul>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT 98</p>
<ul>
<li>One should not have internal fetal heart rate monitoring if she is HIV positive. This is because she may pass on the infection to the baby.</li>
<li>Internal monitoring may make one to have some <strong>slight discomfort</strong> when the electrode is put or inserted in the uterus</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="machine-maintenance-and-inspection">Machine Maintenance and Inspection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#machine-maintenance-and-inspection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="i-visual-inspection-daily">i) Visual Inspection (Daily)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#i-visual-inspection-daily" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Prior to using the monitor, perform the following inspections:</p>
<ul>
<li>Check the monitor and accessories to see if there is any visible evidence of damage that may affect patient safety. Pay special attention to the seams on the transducers and cables before immersing them into conductive fluid.</li>
<li>Check all the outer cables, power socket and power cables.</li>
<li>Check if the monitor functions properly. If any damage is detected, stop using the monitor. Replace the damage part(s).</li>
<li>Make sure all exposed screws are tight.</li>
<li>Check the external cables for splits, cracks or signs of twisting.</li>
<li>Replace any cable that shows serious damage</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ii-routine-inspection">ii) Routine Inspection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ii-routine-inspection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The overall check of the monitor includes; safety check and function check which should be performed by qualified personnel every 6 to 12 months, and each time after service. The equipment should undergo periodic safety testing to ensure proper patient isolation from live parts. This should include leakage current measurement and insulation testing.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="maintenance-of-monitor">Maintenance of Monitor<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maintenance-of-monitor" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Keep the exterior surface of the monitor clean and free of dust and dirt. The appearance of moisture on the screen may occur with abrupt temperature or humidity changes—A stable environment is recommended.</li>
<li>Avoid scratching and damaging the screen.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="maintenance-of-transducer">Maintenance of Transducer<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maintenance-of-transducer" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)</p>
<p>COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
99</p>
<ul>
<li>Keep the transducers in a dry environment, where the temperature should be lower than +45°C (+113 °F).</li>
<li>Gel must be wiped from the transducer after use. These precautions will prolong the life of the transducer.</li>
<li>Avoid contacting the transducers with hard or sharp objects. Although transducers are designed for durability, they should be handled with care. Rough handling could damage the cover, piezoelectric crystals and mechanical movement.</li>
<li>Do not excessively flex the cables.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cleaning-of-monitor">Cleaning of Monitor<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cleaning-of-monitor" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Unplug the monitor from the AC power source, remove the battery and detach all accessories before cleaning.</li>
<li>The solutions recommended for monitor cleaning are: mild soapy water, Ten sides, Ethylate and Acetaldehyde.</li>
<li>Clean the screen with a dry soft cloth.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cleaning-accessories-transducer">Cleaning accessories-Transducer<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cleaning-accessories-transducer" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Wipe them with a soft cloth dampened in cleaning solution; Clean them with a soft cloth dampened in water then Air-dry them or wipe the remaining moisture with a soft dry cloth.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
100</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="endoscopy">ENDOSCOPY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#endoscopy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="how-do-endoscopes-work">How do endoscopes work?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-do-endoscopes-work" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-1451b448.jpeg" alt="img-45.jpeg">
Figure 1. Illustration of how endoscopes work.</p>
<ol>
<li>One of the two main endoscope cables carries light from a bright lamp in the operating room into the body, illuminating the cavity where the endoscope has been inserted.</li>
<li>The light bounces along the walls of the cable into the patient's body cavity.</li>
<li>The diseased or injured part of the patient's body is illuminated by the light shining in.</li>
<li>Light reflected off the body part travels back up a separate fiber-optic cable, bouncing off the glass walls as it goes.</li>
<li>The light shines into the physician's eyepiece so he or she can see what's happening inside the patient's body. Sometimes the fiber-optic cable is directed into a video camera (which displays what's happening on a television monitor) or a CCD (which can capture images like a digital camera or feed them into a computer for various kinds of image enhancement).</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="how-are-fiber-optic-cables-different-in-endoscopes">How are fiber-optic cables different in endoscopes?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-are-fiber-optic-cables-different-in-endoscopes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>You might be wondering what's the difference between fiber-optic cables used in endoscopes and those used for carrying telephone calls, cable TV, and Internet data. Telecommunications cables are designed to carry data in digital form over very long distances; by contrast, the cables used in endoscopes carry pictures over much shorter distances and in analog form. In other words, while telecoms cables carry binary data (long strings of zeros and ones) that represent everything from MP3 music tracks to digital photos of rock stars, endoscope cables carry the actual pictures of someone's insides!</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES -
VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
101</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="medical-endoscope-fiber-optic-construction-and-working">Medical Endoscope - Fiber Optic: Construction and working<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-endoscope-fiber-optic-construction-and-working" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-3b7a95a3.jpeg" alt="img-46.jpeg">
Figure 2. fibre optic endoscope system</p>
<p>Optical fibers are very much useful in medical field. Using low quality, large diameter and short length silica fibers we can design a fiber optic endoscope or fibroscope.</p>
<p>A medical endoscope is a tubular optical instrument, used to inspect or view the internal parts of human body which are not visible to the naked eye. The photograph of the internal parts can also be taken using this endoscope.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="construction">Construction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#construction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Figure 3 shows the structure of endoscope. It has two fibers viz.</p>
<ol>
<li>Outer fiber (f₀)</li>
<li>The inner fiber (fᵢ).</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="outer-fiber">Outer fiber:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#outer-fiber" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The outer fiber consists of many fibers bundled together without any particular order of arrangement and is called incoherent bundle. These fiber bundles as a whole are enclosed in a thin sleeve for protection. The outer fiber is used to illuminate or focus the light onto the inner parts of the body.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="inner-fiber-imaging-fibre-bundle">Inner fiber (Imaging Fibre Bundle):<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#inner-fiber-imaging-fibre-bundle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The inner fiber also consists of a bundle of fibers, but in perfect order. Therefore this arrangement is called coherent bundle. This fiber is used to collect the reflected light from the object. A tiny lens is fixed to one end of the bundle in order to effectively focus the light, reflected from the object. For a wider field of view and better image quality, a telescope system is added in the internal part of the telescope.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES -
VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
102</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-f6453984.jpeg" alt="img-47.jpeg">
Figure 3. Structure of an endoscope</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="working-principle">Working principle:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#working-principle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Light from the source is passed through the outer fiber <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi mathvariant="normal">f</mi><mn>0</mn></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">(\mathrm{f}_0)</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right: 0.07778em;">f</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3011em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: -0.0778em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">0</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span></span>. The light is illuminated on the internal part of the body. The reflected light from the object is brought to focus using the telescope to the inner fiber <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi mathvariant="normal">f</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">(\mathrm{f}_i)</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right: 0.07778em;">f</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3117em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: -0.0778em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">i</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span></span>. Here each fiber picks up a part of the picture from the body. Hence the picture will be collected bit by bit and is transmitted in an order by the array of fibers. As a result, the whole picture is reproduced at the other end of the receiving fiber as shown in the figure. The output is properly amplified and can be viewed through the eye piece at the receiving end.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-6eb80963.jpeg" alt="img-48.jpeg">
Figure 4. Importance of fibre bundle arrangement.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES -
VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
103</p>
<p>The imaging fibre bundle is a key component of a flexible fibre endoscope and determines the image quality. The clearer and more well defined the image quality, the more support it delivers to the diagnosis of the lesion and suggests options for further treatment planning. The challenge is that each single fibre has exactly the same dimension and is positioned at the identical position at both ends of the fibre bundle. If this is not achieved, the image quality is impaired and artifacts disturb the image.</p>
<p>The viewing bundle of a standard fibre-endoscope is 2–3·mm in diameter and contains 20·000–40·000 fine glass fibres, each close to 10·μm in diameter. Light focused onto the face of each fibre is transmitted by repeated internal reflections (fig. 5).</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-de3b9723.jpeg" alt="img-49.jpeg">
Figure 5 Total internal reflection of light down a glass fibre</p>
<p>Faithful transmission of an image depends upon the spatial orientation of the individual fibres being the same at both ends of the bundle (a ‘coherent’ bundle). Each individual glass fibre is coated with glass of a lower optical density to prevent leakage of light from within the fibre, since the coating does not transmit light. This coating and the space between the fibres causes a dark ‘packing fraction’, which is responsible for the fine mesh frequently apparent in the fibreoptic image (Fig. 6).</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-b0f356bd.jpeg" alt="img-50.jpeg">
Figure 6 Fibre bundle showing the ‘packing fraction’ or dead space between fibres.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
104</p>
<p>For this reason, the image quality of a fibreoptic bundle, though excellent, can never equal that of a rigid lens system. However, fibreoptic bundles are extremely flexible, and an image can be transmitted even when tied in a knot. In most modern instruments the distal lens which focuses the image onto the bundle is fixed, and a pin-hole aperture gives a depth of focus from <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>10</mn><mo>−</mo><mn>15</mn><mo>⋅</mo><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">c</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">10 - 15\cdot \mathrm{cm}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">10</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">−</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">15</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">⋅</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4306em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">cm</span></span></span></span></span></span> down to about <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>3</mn><mo>⋅</mo><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">3\cdot \mathrm{mm}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">3</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">⋅</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4306em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">mm</span></span></span></span></span></span>. The image reconstructed at the top of the bundle is transmitted to the eye via a focusing lens, adjustable to compensate for individual differences in refraction.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="anatomy-physiology-of-a-flexible-scope-anatomical-structure">Anatomy &amp; Physiology of a Flexible Scope: Anatomical Structure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anatomy-physiology-of-a-flexible-scope-anatomical-structure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The anatomical structure of the flexible endoscope is the outer shell, composed of five basic sections: light guide connector, light guide tube, control body, insertion tube and bending section. Each section is constructed differently but each has a protective outer layer and hollow inner area that contains the delicate internal systems.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-1c3610b6.jpeg" alt="img-51.jpeg">
Figure 7. Anatomical structure of a flexible endoscope</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-f7f2368e.jpeg" alt="img-52.jpeg">
Figure 8. Details of the internal arrangement of components</p>
<p>Light Guide Connector-The light guide connector is the solid end of the scope that connects to the light source or video cart system. It is the scope section most distant from the patient. On most models it is constructed of molded plastic and metal components with no moving parts. In some models, circuit boards may also be housed. The suction, air, water, light, video system and electrical ground all connect to the scope here. Damage to this part of the endoscope is most often associated with impact and least often with typical day to day use.</p>
<p>Light Guide Tube - Sometimes called the universal cord, this hollow tube connects the light guide connector to the control body. Some videoscope models may have two light guide tubes as the scopes may have separate connections to the light source and video processor. Multiple layers of steel coil, fiber mesh and vulcanized rubber are bonded together to make up this tube. A thin layer of clear polyurethane is applied to the tube for chemical and fluid resistance.</p>
<p>The light guide tube provides protection to the delicate internal components such as suction channels and fiber optics, and it is designed to accept some bending and twisting. However, repeated over-twisting or tight coiling can result in tube damage as well as to the internal components. The diameter and length of the light guide tube is similar on most GI endoscope model</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="list-four-of-the-six-systems-that-connect-through-the-light-guide-connector">List four of the six systems that connect through the light guide connector.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#list-four-of-the-six-systems-that-connect-through-the-light-guide-connector" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES -
VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
105</p>
<ol>
<li>Suction</li>
<li>Air</li>
<li>Water</li>
<li>Light</li>
<li>Video System</li>
<li>Electrical Ground</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="list-three-elements-that-comprise-the-light-guide-tube">List three elements that comprise the light guide tube<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#list-three-elements-that-comprise-the-light-guide-tube" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Steel coil</li>
<li>Fiber mesh</li>
<li>Vulcanized rubber</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Control Body</strong> - This section of the scope contains the physician controls: angulation control knobs, forceps raiser or elevator lifter, air/ water, suction control valves, remote video switches, biopsy port and focus mechanism for fiber optic scopes, tension controller and the control body for holding the endoscope. Most scope models have molded plastic bodies ergonomically designed for ease of use. The remote video switch covers and the angulation control knob seals are the most commonly repaired parts of the control body. The control body is similar size and shape on most GI endoscope models.</p>
<p><strong>Insertion Tube</strong> - The insertion tube is the long flexible tube inserted into the body during normal use. The length and diameter of the insertion tube varies greatly by model as is dependent upon the anatomy viewed. Similar to the light guide tube, it is constructed of multiple layers of steel coil, fiber mesh and vulcanized rubber. The thickness of each layer may vary by model and by tube diameter. A clear protective outer layer is labeled with metric insertion depth marks.</p>
<p>The insertion tube is hollow and provides protection for the delicate internal components including the angulation system, fiber optics, video signal wires and biopsy channel. Sharp bending and over-coiling of the insertion tube will cause damage to the tube itself, and may damage the internal components. The damage is often indicated by raised ridges or buckles appearing along the tube</p>
<p><strong>Bending Section</strong> - Located at the distal end of the insertion tube, the bending section is constructed of articulating steel ribs riveted together to form a flexible skeleton-like shell. The shell is covered with a steel mesh braid and then a thin-walled flexible tube called the bending rubber or sheath. The distal end of the bending section contains the video chip, optical glass lens systems, fiber optics and the termination nozzle of the air/water system. The overall length of the bending section varies by model but it is usually around four inches long. The outside diameter of most gastroscopes, duodenoscopes, and colonoscopes can range from 5.9 to 12.5 mm.</p>
<p>The bending section is the most fragile portion of the flexible endoscope and must be protected from impact. Impact to the distal tip potentially damages all of the inner components.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="name-the-two-layers-of-the-insertion-tube-that-protect-the-fiber-mesh">Name the two layers of the insertion tube that protect the fiber mesh<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#name-the-two-layers-of-the-insertion-tube-that-protect-the-fiber-mesh" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>The steel coil</li>
<li>Vulcanized rubber</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="name-three-of-the-four-components-housed-in-the-distal-tip-of-the-flexible-endoscope">Name three of the four components housed in the distal tip of the flexible endoscope<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#name-three-of-the-four-components-housed-in-the-distal-tip-of-the-flexible-endoscope" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Video chip</li>
<li>Optical glass lens system</li>
<li>Fiber optics</li>
<li>Termination nozzle of the air and water system</li>
</ol>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES – VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
106</p>
<p>Each flexible scope contains a number of internal systems that perform the functions specific to its model. Typically, large-diameter insertion tubes contain more internal components and may potentially have larger operating channels.</p>
<p><strong>Light Transmission</strong> - All flexible endoscopes have a light transmission component for image illumination. The light enters the scope, usually at the light guide connector, through the light guide prong or paddle connector. Some specialty, small-diameter flexible endoscopes have a self-contained battery-powered light source for use when access to a cart system is impractical.</p>
<p>Inside the scope, light travels from the light guide prong to the distal end through a light fiber bundle, a collection of thousands of thin, flexible optical glass fibers. Each individual fiber transports a small portion of light, and together they can produce a very intense bright light. The light exits the scope at the distal end through the light guide lenses, which disperse the light evenly across the visual field. Typical GI scopes have two or three light guide bundles.</p>
<p>There is no adjustment capacity within the light fiber system in the scope. All light adjustments are made manually on the light source or automatically within the video cart system. Damage to the fibers results in reduced light transmission.</p>
<p><strong>Image Capturing</strong> – Imaging is the primary function of the endoscope. An image is captured at the distal end (using the objective lens system) and is then transferred to the image transmission device directly behind the lens system.</p>
<p>Fiber optic endoscopes use an image fiber bundle (similar to the light fiber bundle) to carry the image to an ocular lens at the control body for viewing. Each of the thousands of fibers carries a small portion of the image, and a black dot on the image represents one broken fiber.</p>
<p>Video endoscopes (videoscopes) are more common than fiber optic scopes, and image transmission is by video chip and digital image signal. On video endoscopes, the video chip, a charge coupled device (or CCD) is located directly behind the objective lens assembly at the distal end. Newer technology may use a CMOS video chip (complementary metal oxide semiconductor). Here the image is converted to a digital signal. It travels through signal wires running through the scope to the light guide connector or video connector. The digital signal then connects directly to or through a cable to the video processor on the cart system. The image can be sent to a variety of monitors, printers or remote locations. Endoscope video chips contain from 100,000 to 1 million pixels. More pixels usually mean better image quality, resolution and color reproduction.</p>
<p><strong>Angulation/Wiring System</strong> - All flexible scopes have an angulation system of wires, guided by knobs on the control body. This system manipulates the bending section for insertion and viewing. The knobs are connected inside the control body housing to either a pulley-and-wire system or a gear-and-chain system that connects to the angle wires. The angle wires are braided stainless steel cables that extend from the control body through the insertion tube and connect to the bending ribs at the distal end. Each wire controls one direction of movement, so two opposite wires work together to provide movement up and down, left and right. The angle wires inside the insertion tube are encased within a protective coil pipe that protects the other internal components from the angle wire.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES -
VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
107</p>
<p>Some colonoscope models may contain an additional wiring component to boost the rigidity of the insertion tube. This rigor is provided in three levels and is designed to be neutralized before withdrawing the colonoscope after terminal intubation has been achieved. Excess wear and tear on this wired enhancement is minimized when the stiffness is deactivated for transport, decontamination, reprocessing and storage.</p>
<p><strong>Biopsy/Suction System</strong> - The biopsy and suction channels are part of the same internal system. The biopsy channel is a straight piece of uniform flexible tubing running from the distal end to the control body. The suction channel is similar but runs from the control body to the light guide connector. The suction and biopsy channels are joined in the control body and are controlled by the suction valve controls.</p>
<p>An external suction device connected to the suction channel at the light guide connector provides the suction pressure needed to perform biopsy, and suctioned material then travels back through the biopsy channel at the biopsy port opening.</p>
<p>Some small-diameter specialty scopes do not have a biopsy/suction channel system.</p>
<p><strong>Air/Water System</strong> - The air and water internal channels are thin flexible tubes running from the light guide connector to the distal end. Although air and water flow through separate tubes, they are controlled by the same valve on the control body. Air and water exit the scope at the distal end through the air/water nozzles, which direct the flow over the objective lens. Most small diameter scopes do not have air/water capability.</p>
<p><strong>List three internal systems present in all scopes</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Light transmission</li>
<li>Image capture</li>
<li>Angulation systems</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Forcep Raiser Function</strong> - Some flexible scopes are equipped with a forcep raiser (also called elevator) at the distal end to deflect accessories passed through the biopsy channel. This small metal arm at the biopsy port opening is attached to a wire that runs inside the insertion tube, connects to a control lever on the control body, and operates much like the angulation system controls. The forceps raising function is most commonly found on duodenoscopes and endoscopic ultrasound scopes.</p>
<p><strong>Fluid and Chemical Resistant Seals</strong> – Except for the electrical video connections, the entire outer surface of a flexible scope is chemical and fluid resistant. Any seams between parts are sealed by O-rings, and a standard colonoscope may contain over forty of these O-rings. The chemical- and fluid-resistant coatings on the flexible tubes are themselves flexible, and some parts of the scope are sealed with epoxy. The ends of the bending rubber are sealed with silk or nylon braid and then covered with epoxy. Caps or covers are provided to seal the electrical video connections against fluid. The end result is a device that, when undamaged, can be immersed completely in water or cleaning/disinfecting fluid. In this way, the instrument can be reprocessed over and over.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES -
VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>MATERNITY EQUIPMENT
108</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pill-cam-the-endoscope-of-the-future">Pill cam: the endoscope of the future?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pill-cam-the-endoscope-of-the-future" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Endoscopes are brilliant inventions, but no-one really enjoys having a camera tube stuffed inside them! What's the alternative? In the future, doctors hope to shrink endoscopes to the size of a tiny pill you can swallow. Inside the pill, a miniature camera will pick up images of your insides and a radio transmitter will beam them out to a monitor nearby.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-8e32d638.jpeg" alt="img-54.jpeg">
Figure 2. Illustration of pill-cam.</p>
<p>The top part of the artwork shows how much technology is packed in a pill-cam. Does it sound impossible? Not really! LEDs are smaller than pills and have lenses built into them. CCDs are not much thinner than a piece of card. Watch and calculator batteries are pretty tiny too. And even complex electronic circuits can be made very small and thin. So the whole thing sounds feasible.</p>
<p>And here's how it works:</p>
<ol>
<li>You swallow the pill-cam and it tumbles through your body, taking pictures of damaged or diseased tissue.</li>
<li>The LEDs at the front of the pill-cam fire out enough light to generate an image.</li>
<li>The CCD chip picks up the reflected light and generates a digital image.</li>
</ol>
<p>The radio transmitter sends digital images to a computer outside the body.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING II TEACHING MANUAL (NOTES -
VOLUME 1)
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><div data-testid="stAppIframeResizerAnchor" data-iframe-height="true" class="st-emotion-cache-1dumvfu eht7o1d9"></div></section></div></div></div><div data-testid="portal" id="portal" class="st-emotion-cache-1q6lfs0 e19n7mk11"></div></div><div class=""></div></div>
